# iPad vs Desktop Parity — Raw Consolidated Gap Analysis

This document is the **raw, consolidated gap data** for the xLights iPad app measured against the desktop app, covering 23 functional areas. It was generated from a fresh code-level analysis of `src-iPad/`, the shared `src-core/`, and the desktop `src-ui-wx/` layers. It is the **input to the plan set** — a complete, unedited reference of every feature, its parity status, priority, effort, iPad code location, and the notes/reason behind the call. Downstream planning docs should cite this file rather than re-deriving the data.

**Totals:** 1112 features across 23 areas — 525 implemented, 223 partial, 295 missing, 69 out-of-scope.

Status legend: **implemented** = at functional parity (possibly via a touch idiom); **partial** = present but with real gaps; **missing** = absent but portable; **out-of-scope** = not applicable / not viable on iPad (reason given inline).

## 1. File & Sequence Lifecycle

_Parity summary._ The iPad app has strong parity on the core lifecycle: New (3-step wizard), Open, Save, Save As, Close-with-dirty-prompt, autosave (.xbkp recovery), recent sequences + recent show folders, show-folder switching, and a 6-tab Sequence Settings sheet (Info/Metadata/Media/Timings/Audio/Render) all wired through the shared core via XLSequenceDocument. The biggest true gaps are the backup/restore family (Backup F10, Alternate Backup F11, Restore Backup, Revert To) and Export House Preview Video, none of which exist on iPad yet — backup/restore is straightforward to port (file copying), but video export depends on the wx/FFmpeg VideoExporter which is desktop-only. Several wizard pages (View selection, Import Data, Optional Tasks) and Sequence-Settings pieces (Adjust Milliseconds, Overwrite Media Tags, VAMP timing, Data Layers, Download Sequence/Lyrics) are missing or deferred, and there is no Key Bindings editor (the iPad uses hardware-keyboard shortcuts directly with no remapping UI). Legacy .xml/.fseq open-conversion is desktop-only (wx converter pipeline + ConvertLogDialog).

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| New Sequence command | Implemented | P0 | S | /Users/dkulp/working/xLights/src-iPad/App/NewSequenceWizardView.swift; SequencerViewModel.newSequence (SequencerViewModel.swift:1076); XLSequenceDocument.newSequenceAtPath:type:mediaPath:durationMS:frameMS: (XLSequenceDocument.mm:421) | Fully wired: New launches the 3-step wizard, creates the .xsq via the bridge, hands off to the open path. Reached from the SequencePickerView toolbar (no Cmd-N equivalent in a no-sequence-open state, but the New button is present). |
| New Sequence Wizard - Type page (Musical/Animation/Effect) | Implemented | P1 | S | /Users/dkulp/working/xLights/src-iPad/App/NewSequenceWizardView.swift typePage (line 176), bridgeString maps to Media/Animation/Effect | Radio-style picker for the three types, drives the content page. Functionally equivalent to desktop's bitmap-button page. |
| New Sequence Wizard - media selection (musical) | Implemented | P1 | S | NewSequenceWizardView.swift contentPage musical branch (line 216) + MediaRelocation prompt (line 112); /Users/dkulp/working/xLights/src-iPad/App/MediaRelocation.swift | Musical type asks for an audio file via fileImporter, routes through MediaRelocation to land the file in the show/media folder. Duration is deferred to the media probe on load. Media tags/duration derivation happens in core. |
| New Sequence Wizard - FPS/timing page | Implemented | P1 | S | NewSequenceWizardView.swift contentPage non-musical branch (line 232), frame interval segmented picker 25/50/100 ms (line 247) | Frame interval offered as 25/50/100 ms segmented control. iPad adds 100ms vs desktop's 25/50/Custom; there is no free-form Custom ms entry on the wizard, but frame rate is editable post-create in Sequence Settings > Render. Minor: no arbitrary custom value at wizard time. |

User can adjust membership afterward via the Display Elements sheet (DisplayElementsSheet.swift). Porting would mean adding a wizard page that lists views and seeds the chosen one. Lower value since Display Elements already covers it post-create. |
| New Sequence Wizard - Import Data page | Missing | P3 | M | — | No in-wizard import step. iPad has standalone Import Effects (ImportEffectsView.swift, .xsq/.xsqz/.xml) and SuperStar import post-create, so the capability exists outside the wizard; LOR/HLS/Vixen/Glediator/LSP source importers are desktop-only. A wizard hook would just defer to the existing import sheet. |
| New Sequence Wizard - Optional Tasks / Done page | Missing | P3 | S | — | No Edit Metadata / Import Timings final page; the wizard's last step is the file save. All of these are available post-create (Sequence Settings sheet, row-header timing import). Marginal value. |

Uses the shared core SequenceFile::Open path. Picker is .xsq/.xsqz only — no .fseq or legacy .xml in the open file types. |
| Open: autosave (.xbkp) recovery prompt | Implemented | P1 | S | XLightsApp.swift xbkp recovery sheet (line 193, 691); SequencerViewModel hasRecoverableBackup/applyAutosaveBackup/suppressAutosaveBackup (lines 1631/1654/1682) | On open, compares .xbkp mtime vs .xsq and sheets Recover (promote .xbkp -> .xsq + reopen) or Discard. Implemented at the Swift app layer rather than inside the bridge's OpenSequence (desktop does it in SeqFileUtilities). The analogous rgbeffects .xbkp recovery is handled at the core layer. |
| Open: legacy format conversion / fseq fallback | Missing | P3 | XL | — | iPad opens .xsq (and .xsqz) only. There is no path to open/convert a legacy .xml sequence or read raw .fseq into a sequence — desktop's converter pipeline + ConvertLogDialog is wx-bound and not in src-core. The .xbkp open-with-save-as-xsq-warning is also not surfaced. Marginal for iPad users (new/modern sequences), and the converter would be a large wx-free porting effort. |
| Save command | Implemented | P0 | S | SequencerView.swift Save toolbar button (line 351); SequencerViewModel.saveSequence (line 1372) + coordinatedWrite (NSFileCoordinator); XLSequenceDocument.saveSequence (XLSequenceDocument.h:118) | Writes .xsq (coordinated write) + fseq; dirty-dot indicator; Cmd-S binding in XLightsCommands. Packaged sequences round-trip back into the .xsqz. There is no separate user-configurable fseq folder on iPad (fseq lives beside the xsq); backup-on-save does not exist (no backup feature). |
| Save As Sequence command | Partial | P1 | S | SequencerView.swift Save As (line 267); SequencerViewModel.saveSequenceAs (line 1491); XLSequenceDocument.saveSequenceAs: (XLSequenceDocument.mm:535) | Save As via fileExporter, updates the recent list and display name. Missing the desktop guard that validates the new filename is inside the show directory — on iPad the system file picker can place it anywhere the user has granted access (sandbox/iCloud), and there is no warn-if-outside-show-folder check. Add a show-dir validation to match desktop behavior. |

Clears sequence state and, for packaged sequences, cleans up the temp dir. Equivalent to desktop's SaveChangesDialog flow. |

Presented in the picker rather than a File submenu, which fits the iPad no-sequence-open state. |
| Recent Show Folders | Implemented | P2 | S | /Users/dkulp/working/xLights/src-iPad/App/RecentShowFolders.swift; /Users/dkulp/working/xLights/src-iPad/App/FolderConfigView.swift (Recent Show Folders section, line 79+) | Global MRU of show folders (cap 8) with tap-to-switch and swipe-to-remove, in the Folder config view. | Select Show Folder (permanent switch) | Partial | P1 | M | FolderConfigView.swift (Change Show Folder, line 74; commit at line 328); SequencerViewModel.loadShowFolder (line 886); XLSequenceDocument.loadShowFolder: | Switch the permanent show folder via FolderConfigView (picker + recents), reloading models/networks/effects through the bridge. Missing desktop's validation/warnings (warn if the chosen dir doesn't look like a show folder, or is inside a Backup/Program Files dir). On iPad it just loads whatever was picked. Adding a 'looks like a show folder' heuristic + warning would close the gap. |
| Change Show Folder Temporarily | Missing | P3 | M | — | No temporary-vs-permanent distinction on iPad; switching the folder in FolderConfigView is permanent. The packaged-sequence (.xsqz) open path does load a temp show folder and restore the previous one on close, which is a related but distinct mechanism. Low value on iPad. |
| Backup (F10) | Missing | P1 | M | — | No manual Backup command. There is no timestamped-Backup-subfolder copy of show files on iPad. The pieces needed (FileManager copy of .xsq/.xml/.xbkp/.json/.xmap under a size cap into a Backup/<timestamp> dir, after saving the working file) are pure file ops with no platform blocker; the desktop logic in DoBackup/CopyFiles is straightforward to mirror in Swift or expose via the bridge. Real value for users who keep a single show folder. Sandbox/security-scoped write to the show folder is already handled. |
| Alternate Backup (F11) | Missing | P2 | M | — | No alternate-backup-directory feature. Would require picking and remembering an alternate dir (likely another iCloud/Files location, since external-drive semantics differ on iOS) plus the same copy logic as Backup. Build on top of the Backup port. |
| Backup on launch / on save | Missing | P2 | S | — | No backup-on-launch or backup-on-save preferences (there is no Backup feature to trigger). Once a Backup port exists, adding toggles in FolderConfigView/Render settings is small. Depends on the Backup (F10) work. |
| Restore Backup | Missing | P2 | M | — | No Restore Backup dialog. Pairs with the Backup port: list Backup/<timestamp> subfolders, pick files to copy back into the show folder, reload. Requires sequence be closed first (same as desktop). Pure file/UI work, no platform blocker. |
| Revert To... versioned backups (macOS) | Out-of-scope | P3 | L | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: macOS-only NSDocument/NSFileVersion revision API; iOS has no equivalent automatic file-version history for app-managed files outside iCloud's own version store, which isn't exposed the same way. — Desktop's Revert To uses macOS NSFileVersion document-revision APIs (GetFileRevisions/GetURLForRevision). iOS does not provide the same on-disk versioned-revision browser for arbitrary sandboxed files. |
| Export House Preview Video | Out-of-scope | P2 | XL | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: Desktop encoder lives in wx-only src-ui-wx and relies on FFmpeg encode (not in src-core). iPad could in principle build an AVAssetWriter exporter from the Metal house preview, but that is net-new XL work with no shared-core reuse, so it's effectively out-of-scope for parity rather than a simple wiring task. — No video export on iPad. The desktop VideoExporter (/Users/dkulp/working/xLights/src-ui-wx/media/VideoExporter.cpp) is wx-dependent and uses FFmpeg encode. A native AVAssetWriter-based exporter feeding frames from the house-preview Metal canvas would be a large new subsystem. |

VAMP plugins are loadable C++ libraries; bundling/loading them on iOS is fraught (App Store dynamic-library policy, same constraint that disables AI plugins), so the native analysis path is the right substitute. Low priority. |

Note .pgo import is desktop-import-only on desktop but iPad supports it here — slight superset. The settings-sheet comment about deferring import/export is stale; it is actually present. |

No render-mode (Erase/Canvas) selection, data-layer import/delete/reorder/re-import. Data layers are a niche imported-rendering feature; the core data-layer model is shared, so a future port is wiring + a tree UI, but value is low for typical iPad users. |
| Sequence Settings - Download Sequence and Lyrics | Missing | P3 | L | — | No VendorMusicDialog equivalent to download a matching sequence + lyrics for the loaded song. iPad does have online lyric search (LRCLIB) for timing tracks, which covers the lyrics half. The full sequence-download-from-vendor flow is not present; depends on the vendor music repository API (shareable core, but UI is net-new). Marginal. |
| Key Bindings editor | Missing | P3 | L | — | No KeyBindingEditDialog equivalent — shortcuts are hard-coded in XLightsCommands.swift with no remap UI or persistence of custom bindings. Hardware-keyboard shortcuts work, but the user cannot view/remap them. A remap editor is feasible (read the same KeyBindings core) but is a sizeable new UI for a feature most touch-first iPad users won't reach for. Low priority. |
| Lifecycle keyboard shortcuts (built-in accelerators) | Partial | P1 | S | /Users/dkulp/working/xLights/src-iPad/App/XLightsCommands.swift (File: Close Cmd-W, Save Cmd-S, Save As Shift-Cmd-S, Sequence Settings; Playback: Render All Cmd-R, etc.) | Has Save (Cmd-S), Save As (Shift-Cmd-S), Close (Cmd-W), Sequence Settings, Render All (Cmd-R) on a connected hardware keyboard. Missing the lifecycle accelerators that have no iPad menu home: New (Cmd-N is in the picker as a button, not a hardware shortcut while a sequence is open), Open (Cmd-O — opening goes through the picker, not a key), and there is no F10/F11 Backup (no backup feature). Add Cmd-N/Cmd-O hardware bindings once their flows are reachable mid-session. |
| Open New xLights Instance | Out-of-scope | P3 | M | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: iOS apps are single-process; you cannot spawn a second independent application instance. Multi-scene windows exist but share one process/app state, so a truly separate second instance isn't possible on iPad. — iPad does support multiple windows (WindowGroup scenes for previews/inspector), but launching a second independent instance of the whole app with its own document is not an iOS concept the way it is on desktop. |
| Preferences entry point | Partial | P2 | M | /Users/dkulp/working/xLights/src-iPad/App/FolderConfigView.swift (show/media/fseq folders, recents); SequenceSettingsSheet.swift RenderTab (autosave interval, blending, frame rate); AIServicesSettingsSheet.swift | No single Preferences (Cmd-,) panel. Settings are scattered: FolderConfigView (folders), Sequence Settings > Render (autosave interval), AI Services settings. Missing dedicated config for video export codec/bitrate (no video export) and a unified backup-on-save/launch toggle (no backup). A consolidated Preferences screen would improve discoverability but the individual knobs that apply to iPad mostly exist. |
| Quit / app exit with save guard | Implemented | P1 | S | XLightsApp.swift scenePhase handlers quiesceForInactive/shutdownForBackground (lines 89-107) + saveSequence on inactive (line 467); SequencerViewModel.shutdownForBackground | iOS has no explicit Quit; the scene-phase lifecycle does a silent save on inactive/background so work isn't lost (stronger than desktop's prompt — it just saves). F-5 detach-state snapshot/restore on background. This is the correct iPad idiom for the app-exit save guard. |
| Read-only mode guard | Missing | P3 | S | — | No read-only show-folder mode on iPad; New/Open/Save/SaveAs are never blocked by a read-only flag. The desktop guard exists to protect a locked/shared show; on iPad, write access is governed by sandbox/security-scoped bookmarks instead (a failed coordinated write surfaces an error). Could add a parallel read-only flag, but marginal — the platform's access model already prevents writes the user lacks permission for. |

## 2. Edit Operations

_Parity summary._ The iPad has strong parity on the high-frequency edit operations: undo/redo, copy/cut/paste, duplicate, delete, all seven alignment modes, close-gap, split, lock/disable, reset/randomize-settings, description editing, create-timing-from-effects, and row/model copy/cut/paste are all wired (mostly in SequencerViewModel.swift + grid/row-header SwiftUI menus). Notably the iPad does NOT use the core UndoManager for sequencer edits — it uses SwiftUI's closure-based UndoManager (per-op registration), and the desktop's descriptive undo labels are reduced to static "Undo"/"Redo" menu text. The real parity gaps are the bulk/dialog-driven tools that desktop offers as Edit-menu items: Color Replace, the three Shift Effects variants, Find Possible Source Effects, Create Random Effects (fill empty cells), Copy Layers/SubModels to Models (bulk distribution), and a global Select All / Select All No Timing — none of which exist on iPad yet, though several have ready core support (e.g. SequenceElements::GetUsedColours/ReplaceColours).

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Undo | Partial | P0 | M | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift:5234 (undo()), XLightsCommands.swift:60-63, SequencerView.swift:478; memory cap via src-iPad/Bridge/iPadRenderContext.cpp:73 (SetMaxSteps(50)) | Undo works and is bound to Cmd-Z, but the iPad sequencer does NOT use the core src-core/render/UndoManager — it registers per-op closures on SwiftUI's Foundation UndoManager (registerUndo(withTarget:)) with grouping for bulk ops. Each mutating op in the view model hand-rolls its own inverse closure. Two consequences vs desktop: (1) the Edit-menu label is the static string 'Undo' rather than a descriptive label ('Undo Move Effect') — setActionName is called but the Button label is hardcoded; (2) every new mutating op must remember to register an inverse closure or it becomes silently non-undoable (e.g. toggleElementRenderDisabled is explicitly 'Not undo-able in first cut'). Core UndoManager's grouped UNDO_MARKER labels are not surfaced. Effort is to wire the menu label to undoManager.undoActionName and audit ops for missing registrations. |
| Redo | Partial | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift:5235 (redo()), XLightsCommands.swift:65-67 | Redo works via Cmd-Shift-Z on the Foundation UndoManager. Same caveat as Undo: the menu label is the static 'Redo' rather than a descriptive step label (undoManager.redoActionName is available and could be shown). Inherits the per-op closure architecture, so redo fidelity depends entirely on each op registering its inverse correctly. |
| Copy effects (clipboard) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift:5382 (copySelectedEffect), :5397 (copySelectedEffects), :5251-5301 (UIPasteboard publish/sync with custom UTI, B99); grid menu SequencerGridV2View.swift:599 | Copies selected effects to UIPasteboard with a custom xLights UTI (name/settings/palette/row+time offsets), with Universal Clipboard cross-device support. Functionally matches desktop's CopyFormat1 encoding for the iPad's needs. |
| Cut effects | Partial | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift:4569 (cutRow), :4584 (cutModel); XLightsCommands.swift:57-59 | Cut exists for whole rows/models via the row-heading menu (copy then delete). But per-effect Cut (the desktop Edit>Cut / Ctrl-X on a selection) is intentionally omitted from the Edit menu (comment: 'Cut intentionally omitted; disabled-but-bound shortcuts still swallow key events'). Users can copy+delete manually. Low effort to add a Cut entry that calls copySelectedEffects then deleteSelectedEffects in one undo group. No AC-mode zeroing (AC mode not on iPad). |
| Paste effects | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift:5513 (pasteEffect), :5484 (pasteEffectReplacingOverlaps with overwrite confirm), :5593 (pasteAtRow auto-inserts layers); XLightsCommands.swift:85 | Paste reconstructs effects from the pasteboard, applies per-entry row/time offsets, validates overlap per-effect, offers an overwrite confirmation, and auto-grows the destination element's layers when the clipboard spans more rows (mirrors EffectsGrid::PasteModelEffectsWithLayers / PR #6363). Fully wired. |
| Paste By Cell vs Paste By Time (mode toggle) | Partial | P2 | M | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift:5520-5551 (auto paste-by-cell, B14), :4991 (activeTimingCell) | iPad does paste-by-cell automatically: a single-entry clipboard pasted where an active timing track brackets the target time stretches to fill that cell; otherwise it falls through to paste-by-time (relative offsets). There is no user-facing toggle and no persisted mode — the behavior is inferred. Desktop exposes mutually-exclusive toolbar buttons + keybindings letting the user force one mode. Adding an explicit toggle (and honoring it in pasteEffect) is the gap. |
| Paste As Layers mode (+ Alternate Paste) | Partial | P3 | M | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift:5593 (pasteAtRow auto layer-insert) | iPad's pasteAtRow always grows layers to fit a multi-row clipboard (effectively a single 'paste as layers' behavior). There is no persisted xLightsPasteAsLayers preference, no relative-to-single-layer alternative, and no ALTERNATE_PASTE one-off inverse. Marginal for touch workflows; would need a pref + branch in the paste path. |
| Duplicate effect | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift:5430 (duplicateSelectedEffect); XLightsCommands.swift:95 (Cmd-D); grid context menu | Duplicates a single or multi-selection by copying then pasting just after the original(s), preserving the prior clipboard. Plus a numeric-entry sheet (rounded to frame interval). Not undoable on desktop either. Medium because the shift+truncate logic must be ported, not just bridged. |
| Shift Effects (not timing) | Missing | P2 | M | — | Same as Shift Effects And Timing but skips timing tracks (ELEMENT_TYPE_TIMING). Desktop src-ui-wx/xLightsMain.cpp:5892. Note this caps the CORE UndoManager (used for the bridge ops like ConvertEffectsToPerModel), which is separate from the Foundation UndoManager driving the SwiftUI Cmd-Z path. |

## 3. Tools Menu

_Parity summary._ The iPad app covers the highest-value Tools items well: Check Sequence, Package Sequence, FPP Connect, Batch Render, and View Log are all wired through the shared src-core engine, and FPP Connect in particular is richer than the capability map suggested (per-instance Media/Models/UDP-Out/Cape/Proxies/Playlist options). However several Tools entries are entirely absent (Cleanup File Locations, Download Sequences/Lyrics, Export Effects CSV, Purge Download Cache) and a few are only partially realized (no bulk multi-controller upload dialog, no full XLSX controller-connection workbook, no per-check disable preferences, thinner Batch Render and FPP device-management UI). HinksPix export and Lua/Python automation are the only genuinely out-of-scope items — HinksPix needs removable-media/USB writing plus foreign-controller targeting, and running user automation scripts conflicts with App Store policy against interpreted code. Overall this is moderate-to-good parity on the core workflows but with a meaningful tail of portability/export/maintenance utilities still missing.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Check Sequence (run + report) | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/CheckSequenceSheet.swift; src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm runSequenceCheckWithProgress:; src-iPad/Bridge/XLCheckSequenceIssue.{h,mm}; core src-core/diagnostics/SequenceChecker | Async run with progress, grouped-by-severity issues, severity+section filter chips, and tap-to-jump to the offending effect. Drives the same core SequenceChecker as desktop. iPad surfaces issues in a native sheet rather than the desktop HTML report (an acceptable platform idiom). The core checker omits desktop's wx-only OS/network/prefs sections, but the substantive controller/model/sequence/file checks are present. |
| Check Sequence per-check disable toggles | Partial | P3 | S | src-iPad/App/CheckSequenceSheet.swift (filterChipsRow) | iPad has severity/section filter chips that hide issues in the displayed list, but there is no persisted per-check SUPPRESSION preference (DupUniverse, NonContigCh, PreviewGroup, DupNodeMG, TransTime, CustomSize, SketchImage). The core SequenceCheckerCallbacks::IsCheckOptionDisabled hook exists and is shared; iPad would just need a settings store + a DesktopCheckCallbacks-equivalent on the bridge to feed it. Low value since the view-side filtering already lets users de-clutter the report. |

| Batch Render Force High Definition | Missing | P2 | S | — | iPadRenderContext hard-codes IsLowDefinitionRender()==true, so every iPad render (including batch) is low-definition; there is no Force High Definition checkbox. This is the bigger story: iPad cannot currently produce full-resolution renders at all. Exposing a high-def override (at least for batch/FPP export where memory headroom allows) would need iPadRenderContext to make low-def configurable and the batch UI to surface the toggle. Marked missing (not out-of-scope) because the constraint is a deliberate perf default, not a hard platform limit; effort is small for the checkbox but the underlying low-def behavior is intentional and may need memory guards. |

| HinksPix Export | Out-of-scope | P3 | XL | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: HinksPix export's primary output is writing HSEQ/playlists/schedule to a removable SD/USB card (with a Refresh USB Drives picker). iOS provides no API to enumerate/write raw removable drives, and HinksPix uses proprietary (non-open) controller firmware/protocol, which is outside the FPP/ESPixelStick open-firmware scope the iPad bridge deliberately limits itself to. Combined with the foreign-controller daughter-board targeting, this is a desktop-only workflow. — No iPad implementation. The export-to-controller-over-network leg could in principle be ported, but the dominant SD/USB-card output path is not viable. |

| HinksPix Export to SD Card vs Upload to controller (Refresh USB Drives) | Out-of-scope | P3 | L | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: iOS exposes no API to enumerate or write to raw removable SD/USB drives (the 'Refresh USB Drives'/'Export to SD Card' path), so the primary HinksPix output channel cannot be implemented on iPad. — Part of HinksPix Export; not present on iPad. |
| Run Scripts (Lua / Python automation) | Out-of-scope | P3 | XL | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: Running user-supplied/downloaded interpreted scripts (Lua VM, Python) that drive the app conflicts with App Store Review guideline 2.5.2 (apps may not download or execute code that changes app behavior). The whole point of the feature is executing arbitrary downloaded community scripts, which is exactly what's prohibited. Embedding a sandboxed Lua engine for built-in-only scripts could be argued, but the user-download library management makes the feature as designed out of scope. — No Lua/Python automation runner on iPad (verified: no LuaRunner/PythonRunner/ScriptsDialog references in src-iPad). |
| Run Scripts library management (refresh / view / download) | Out-of-scope | P3 | M | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: Downloading additional community automation scripts to execute is the App-Store-prohibited behavior (2.5.2); the library management exists only to feed the script runner that can't ship. — Subordinate to Run Scripts; not present on iPad. |
| Export Effects (CSV) | Missing | P2 | M | — | No iPad equivalent. The desktop ExportEffects/ExportElement/ExportNodes logic lives in xLightsMain.cpp (not src-core), so this needs either a small core extraction + bridge method or a Swift-side walk over the existing effect-enumeration bridge (effectNamesForRow:/effectStartTimesForRow:/effectSettingsForRow:/visibleRowCount etc., all already exposed) writing a CSV to the share sheet. All the data is already reachable from the bridge, so a Swift reimplementation is straightforward. Useful for documentation/analysis. |
| Export Controller Connections (XLSX) | Partial | P2 | L | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h exportWiringCSVForController:/exportWiringJSONForController: (per-controller, wraps UDController::ExportAsCSV) | iPad can export a SINGLE controller's wiring as CSV or JSON (Phase J-32.7), but lacks the desktop color-coded multi-controller XLSX workbook (one block per controller, smart-remote shading, ExportSettings column options) built with libxlsxwriter. To reach parity iPad would need to loop all controllers and either generate XLSX (libxlsxwriter is in-tree and wx-free, so usable from a bridge) or settle for a combined multi-sheet CSV. The per-controller CSV/JSON already covers the data; the workbook formatting is the gap. |
| View Log | Implemented | P2 | S | src-iPad/App/LogViewerSheet.swift (live spdlog tail with level filter Trace+/Debug+/Info+/Warn+/Error) | iPad provides a live in-app log viewer with a level filter rather than opening the log in an external text viewer (the desktop approach doesn't translate to iOS, where there's no general default text viewer for an app's sandboxed log). Functionally meets or exceeds the desktop intent. Package Logs (share-sheet zip of logs+diagnostics) is also present as a complementary entry. |
| Purge Download Cache | Missing | P3 | S | — | No iPad menu entry to clear the CachedFileDownloader cache. iPad already uses CachedFileDownloader (XLVendorCatalog model download, vendor image fetch), so the underlying ClearCache exists in shared core; this is just a small bridge method + a menu item/share-of-nothing action. Marginal value but trivial to add for disk hygiene / forcing fresh vendor downloads. |

## 4. View / Windows / Perspectives

_Parity summary._ The iPad app replaces the desktop's wxAUI dock/float/perspective model with a fixed SwiftUI split-pane layout (preview band + Metal grid + 4-tab inspector sidebar) plus iPadOS WindowGroup "detach to scene" for House Preview, Model Preview, and each inspector tab. Core sequencer windows reach reasonable parity through different idioms: timeline zoom (in/out/presets), preview/inspector toggles, Display Elements editor, and the four effect property panels (Effect/Colors/Blending/Buffer inspector tabs) are all implemented. The entire desktop "Perspectives" subsystem (save/save-as/edit/auto-save/quick-switch/dynamic menu) is absent and is genuinely out-of-scope because it serializes wxAUI pane geometry that has no iPad analog. The remaining gaps are minor dockable utility panels (Effect Dropper, Jukebox, Search Effects, Video Preview, Find Data, Effect Presets tree, Select Effect, Effect Assist) and two grid-draw toggles (AC Lights toolbar, Show AC Ramps), most of which are P2/P3 since their core function is already reachable via touch idioms or are hardcoded on.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Timeline Zoom In | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/XLightsCommands.swift (XLZoomCommands, lines 556-602: 'Zoom In' Cmd-=, t.pixelsPerMS * 1.5 capped at 2.0); also pinch-zoom in EffectsMetalGridView.swift via TimelineState | Implemented via menu (Cmd-=), pinch gesture, and Zoom To presets. Drives view-owned TimelineState.pixelsPerMS rather than PanelTimeLine, but functionally equivalent. |
| Timeline Zoom Out | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/XLightsCommands.swift (XLZoomCommands, 'Zoom Out' Cmd--, t.pixelsPerMS / 1.5 floored at 0.005) | Implemented via menu, pinch, and an 8-stop 'Zoom To...' preset menu (vs desktop's 19-step ladder, deliberately simplified for touch). Full parity for the user-facing capability. |
| Reset Toolbars | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: iPad has no wxAUI toolbars to reset. The toolbar set is a fixed SwiftUI layout and a menu bar; there is no draggable/dockable AUI toolbar state to persist or restore, so the command has nothing to act on. — No grep hits for any toolbar-reset on iPad. |
| AC Lights Toolbar (AC quick-paint mode) | Missing | P2 | L | — | No ACLights references in src-iPad (only TreePerspective model property unrelated). The AC quick-paint mode (Off/On/Shimmer/Twinkle/Intensity/Ramp + Fill/Cascade + Parm1/Parm2 click-drag painting of On-style effects) is entirely absent. Core AC logic lives in src-ui-wx, not src-core, so this would need both core extraction (or reimplementation) and a SwiftUI touch-paint surface. Touch drag-paint is actually a natural iPad idiom, but the AC mode state machine and the toolbar UI are substantial new work. |
| Show AC Ramps | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/App/EffectsMetalGridView.swift line 577 (appendEffectBackground ... drawRamps: true); bridge XLSequenceDocument.mm line 10096-10135 | Ramps are ALWAYS drawn on iPad (drawRamps hardcoded true) — there is no checkable toggle to flatten On/Twinkle effects back to flat blocks. | Perspectives: Save Current | Out-of-scope | P3 | M | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: A perspective is a wxAUI SavePerspective() geometry string describing dock/float/tab/size of ~17 panes. iPad has no AUI manager and a fixed split-pane layout (only Preview/Inspector toggles + detach-to-scene), so there is no arbitrary pane geometry to capture. The iPad equivalents (pane widths/heights, detached-scene state) are already persisted via @AppStorage automatically. — No perspective save/serialize anywhere in src-iPad. |

Named layout presets would require building an entirely new iPad-side layout-state model (which panes detached, sidebar widths) and a persistence/switch UI — not a port of any shared core, and of low value given the constrained iPad layout. — No named-perspective creation on iPad. |
| Perspectives: Edit/Load (Perspectives manager panel) | Out-of-scope | P3 | L | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: The Perspectives manager add/delete/rename/save/load list operates on wxAUI perspective strings stored in rgbeffects. With no AUI docking on iPad there is nothing for it to manage. Could be re-conceived as named iPad-layout presets but that is net-new design, not a parity port. — PerspectivesPanel.cpp has no iPad counterpart. |
| Perspectives: Auto Save (per-machine) | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | src-iPad/App/SequencerView.swift @AppStorage previewPaneHeight/inspectorPaneWidth; XLightsApp.swift F-5 detach-state snapshot/restore | OUT-OF-SCOPE: The desktop feature auto-saves a wxAUI perspective string per machine. iPad has no AUI string; its analogous live-layout persistence (pane sizes, which scenes are detached) is already always-on and handled natively, so a toggle for it is both unnecessary and inapplicable. — iPad already auto-persists its (much smaller) layout surface — pane sizes via @AppStorage and detached-scene set via the F-5 snapshot/restore in XLightsApp.swift. |
| Perspectives: dynamic per-perspective menu list / quick switch | Out-of-scope | P3 | M | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: Depends entirely on the saved-perspectives list, which does not exist on iPad (no AUI). Nothing to populate the radio-item submenu from. — No perspective menu on iPad. |

| Windows: Jukebox toggle | Missing | P3 | M | — | No Jukebox panel in src-iPad. Could be ported as a SwiftUI grid of slots over the existing preset/effect-copy machinery; moderate. Low priority for a sequencer-focused iPad. |
| Windows: Find Effect Data toggle | Missing | P3 | M | — | No FindData panel in src-iPad. The desktop panel inspects rendered per-channel/per-pixel values at a time point. iPad already drives the full render engine and has pixelDataAtMS/setModelColorsAtMS in the bridge, so the data is available; a SwiftUI inspector panel over that data is the missing piece. Diagnostic feature, low priority. |
| View menu checkmark sync | Implemented | P3 | S | src-iPad/App/XLightsCommands.swift (View group toggles label between Hide/Show Preview and Hide/Show Inspector based on viewModel.showPreview/showInspector; XLPreviewDetachCommands/XLInspectorDetachCommands flip Detach<->Dock and Open<->Dock based on detached state) | Equivalent behavior: menu items reflect live state by switching their title (Hide/Show, Detach/Dock, Open/Dock) rather than a checkmark. | Perspective layout engine (wxAUI dock/float/persist) | Out-of-scope | P2 | XL | src-iPad/App/SequencerView.swift (fixed split-pane), XLightsApp.swift (WindowGroup detach scenes), @AppStorage layout persistence | OUT-OF-SCOPE: wxAUI arbitrary docking/floating/tabbing with serialized perspective strings (and the macOS gray-Metal re-dock workaround) is a wxWidgets-desktop construct with no iPadOS equivalent — iPadOS windowing is scene-based (Stage Manager / Split View), not free-form docking. The capability is intentionally re-implemented with platform-native idioms rather than ported; building a true AUI-style dock manager in SwiftUI would be an enormous effort against the grain of the platform. — iPad replaces the AUI engine with a fixed SwiftUI split-pane + native multi-window (WindowGroup) detach; pane sizes and detach-state persist via @AppStorage and the F-5 snapshot/restore. |

## 5. Setup / Controllers Configuration Tab

_Parity summary._ The iPad has a surprisingly complete controller editor, but it lives inside the Layout Editor's "Controllers" sidebar tab (LayoutEditorView.swift) rather than a dedicated Setup tab — there is no top-level Setup screen. Core CRUD (add Ethernet/Serial/Null, delete, reorder, activate/xLights-only/inactivate, unlink-from-base), the full common + network + serial property grid, network discovery with mismatch resolution, real input/output upload (gated to open-source firmware), an interactive visualizer with drag-drop model assignment and per-model connection editing, and "open web UI" are all wired through real src-core code via XLSequenceDocument. The genuine gaps are protocol-level Ethernet output tuning (Start Universe / Universe Count / Channels-per-Universe / Individual Sizes, DDP/ZCPP/KiNET/OPC/Twinkly specifics — none exposed in controllerPropertiesForName), global output settings (controller sync, sync universe, max-dup-suppress, global proxy/force-local-IP), live ping/status LEDs, Test Lights, Bulk/multi-controller upload, sort, select-all, delete-all, and temporary-show-folder/MRU switching. Most missing pieces are pure SwiftUI+bridge wiring over already-shared core, so effort is generally low-to-medium; the larger items are the universe-output property grid and a PixelTest equivalent.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Set permanent show directory | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/FolderConfigView.swift, src-iPad/App/FolderConfig.swift; bridge XLSequenceDocument.mm loadShowFolder: | FolderConfigView lets the user choose/change the show folder via the iOS document picker, persists it (FolderConfig.showFolderKey + security-scoped bookmark) and reloads controllers/models via viewModel.loadShowFolder. Closing the open sequence on switch is handled in the view model. Full parity. |
| Change show directory temporarily | Missing | P3 | M | — | FolderConfigView only does a permanent switch (writes showFolderKey). No 'open temporarily without making it default' toggle nor the backup/Program-Files warning. Marginal on iPad where folder switching is rarer; would need a transient-path mode in FolderConfig that doesn't persist the bookmark as default. |

Equivalent to the desktop MRU menu (also surfaced in SequencePickerView per the app-views map). |

Low value; DMX serial output is itself constrained on iPad. |
| Upload output configuration to controller | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift startControllerUpload / ControllerUploadModifier (lines 800-804, 1229); bridge uploadOutputForController: → BaseController::SetOutputs (XLSequenceDocument.mm:12986) | Real output upload via the shared BaseController factory + SetOutputs, with FPP-proxy/IP pre-flight (GetResolvedIP) and a connect check; recalcs start channels first like desktop. Gated in the UI to open-source-firmware controllers (caps.openSourceFirmware) — i.e. FPP/ESPixelStick — which is a deliberate scope choice (closed-firmware uploaders not shipped), not a hard platform limit. High-value path implemented. |
| Upload input (universe) configuration to controller | Implemented | P1 | S | bridge uploadInputForController: → BaseController::SetInputUniverses (XLSequenceDocument.mm:12978); LayoutEditorView.swift uploadInput referenced in startControllerUpload | Real input-universe upload via SetInputUniverses, same connect/IP pre-flight. The map notes startControllerUpload calls both uploadInput and uploadOutput. Same open-source-firmware gating as output upload. |
| Bulk / multi controller upload | Missing | P2 | M | — | No multi-controller checklist upload (desktop's MultiControllerUploadDialog). Per-controller upload already exists, so this is a SwiftUI checklist sheet that loops uploadOutput/uploadInputForController: across selected controllers with progress — pure UI+bridge wiring over existing methods. Useful once a user has several FPP devices. |
| FPP Connect (upload sequences/configs to FPP) | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/FPPConnectSheet.swift, FPPAuthPrompt.swift; bridge discoverFPPInstances/applyConfigToFPP:/uploadFseq:toFPPInstances: (XLSequenceDocument) | Full FPP Connect: discover instances, select instances + fseq, per-instance playlist (incl. create-new), cape/proxy/models/UDP config, parallel multi-target fseq upload with progress + auth. Limited to FPP 9+/ESPixelStick (open-source firmware) per the bridge note — a scope choice, not a platform block. High-value path implemented. |
| Open controller web UI / proxy in browser | Implemented | P2 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift LayoutEditorControllerDetailView 'Open' button + onOpenURL UIApplication.shared.open (lines 10550-10559, 2160); row context menu 'Open <ip>' (line 1820) | Per-controller Open button and row context-menu launch the controller's http://<ip>/ web UI in Safari. The dedicated 'Open Proxy' / global-proxy-URL routing is not separately surfaced, but the primary open-web-UI is implemented. |
| Global output settings (sync, suppress frames, force local IP, global proxy) | Missing | P2 | M | — | When no controller is selected the iPad shows an empty-hint, not the desktop global property grid (Controller Sync, E1.31 Sync Universe, Max Duplicate Frames To Suppress, Global Force Local IP, Global FPP Proxy). These are OutputManager-level settings in shared core, so the work is a 'no selection' descriptor set + setter branch reading/writing OutputManager globals. Matters for multi-controller sync output from iPad. |
| Test lights (PixelTestDialog) | Missing | P2 | XL | — | No test-lights UI; XLightsCommands.swift only has a comment noting it as future. iPad CAN drive sACN/ArtNet/DDP/E1.31 output (startOutput/outputFrame are real), so test patterns over network are technically feasible. But PixelTestDialog is a large wx dialog (TestFunctions enum, many chase/shimmer/twinkle/cycle modes, per-channel selection tree, sliders) with no shared-core extraction — would need both a new SwiftUI test panel and a core/bridge test-pattern engine. Serial/DMX test output specifically is out of scope (no host serial port). |
| Output to lights toggle | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/SequencerView.swift output toggle (lines 426-433); SequencerViewModel.swift toggleOutput/sendOutputFrame (1707-1709, 2333-2350); bridge startOutput/stopOutput/isOutputting/outputFrame: (real OutputManager) | Sequencer toolbar toggle opens active controller outputs and streams live frames over sACN/ArtNet/DDP/E1.31 via the real OutputManager. This is network output (the platform-feasible subset); USB/serial DMX output is the only piece that can't work on iOS. Full parity for network protocols. |
| Save controller/network configuration | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift Save (hasUnsavedChanges) → saveLayoutChanges; bridge saveLayoutChanges → iPadRenderContext::SaveLayoutChanges (iPadRenderContext.cpp:448 → OutputManager::Save) | Controller/network edits set hasUnsavedLayoutChanges and are persisted by SaveLayoutChanges, which calls OutputManager::Save() (writes the networks file) and recalcs start channels. The Layout Editor Save button is the iPad equivalent of desktop's Save Setup. Full parity for persistence. |
| Export / import controller connections | Missing | P3 | M | — | No export/import of model-to-controller connection mappings (desktop Tools menu). The visualizer exports per-controller wiring CSV/JSON, but not the full sharable connections export/import. Low value; the desktop logic lives in xLightsMain (wx), so some extraction would be needed. |
| Base show folder linking & unlink | Implemented | P3 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift unlinkControllerFromBase usage; FolderConfigView.swift baseShowDirectory/autoUpdateFromBaseShowDirectory; bridge unlinkControllerFromBase: + baseShowDirectory (XLSequenceDocument.h:2239) | Base-show-folder is configured in FolderConfigView (auto-update/merge), and controllers can be unlinked from base via unlinkControllerFromBase:. The blue read-only coloring for from-base controllers may not be surfaced in the row UI (verify), but the unlink action and base-folder wiring exist. |
| Bulk-edit controller connection / per-port attributes | Partial | P2 | M | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift cc.* Controller Connection descriptor rows (4321-4470); MultiSelectActionBar (bulk property edit per layout-editor map) | Per-model controller-connection editing (protocol, gamma, color order, group count, direction, start/end nulls, brightness, smart-remote id/type) is fully wired in the model properties pane. A dedicated cross-selection bulk-edit dialog like desktop's ControllerConnectionDialog (apply one attribute to many selected models at once) is not confirmed for connection attributes specifically; layout multi-select bulk edit exists for geometry. So single-model parity is complete, multi-model connection bulk-edit is partial. |
| Recalculate start channels & channel-to-controller mapping | Implemented | P1 | S | bridge: ModelManager::RecalcStartChannels called in upload pre-flight (XLSequenceDocument.mm:12957) and SaveLayoutChanges; shared src-core ModelManager | Start-channel recalculation runs via the shared ModelManager (RecalcStartChannels) on save and before upload, identical core logic to desktop. Channel-to-controller resolution is core-shared. No iPad-specific gap, though it is invoked at fewer explicit points than desktop's DoWork dispatcher. |
| IP entry / manual address dialog | Partial | P3 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift controller property pane IP string field; upload uses GetResolvedIP and errors if IP unset (XLSequenceDocument.mm:12944-12949) | There's no dedicated 'prompt for IP at upload time' dialog like desktop's IPEntryDialog; instead upload fails with a message telling the user to set the IP in the property pane first. Functionally the user can always set the IP, just not via an inline prompt. Minor. |

## 6. Layout: Model Creation & Management

_Parity summary._ The iPad's Layout Editor (`LayoutEditorView.swift`, ~12.5K lines, backed by ~30 Phase-J bridge methods) is the most complete iPad subsystem and reaches strong parity on the daily-driver layout flow: model creation (16 model types), .xmodel import (single + multi), vendor download, ARKit Map-from-Lights, tap/drag/resize/rotate/nudge editing, multi-select align/distribute/match-size/flip/duplicate/group, a full per-model + per-type + controller-connection property editor (including start-channel and smart-remote), layout undo, group CRUD with full group settings (layout/grid/center-offset/camera/tag/members), view-object creation/editing, layout-group (preview) switching/creation, search/sort sidebars, 2D/3D toggle, and show-name/info overlays. Genuine gaps are mostly export/diagnostic and a few power-user operations: no model clipboard copy/cut/paste, no Replace-Model, no per-model Node Layout / Wiring diagram, no export-as-custom/.xmodel/CAD, no rgbeffects/LOR-S5 model import, no make-start-channels-valid fixer, no preview rename/delete, no save/print layout image, no model-unlink-from-base, and the Views&Models panel lacks desktop's full sort/master-import menu. Most of these are pure SwiftUI+bridge wiring over already-shared `src-core/` logic; only CAD export and layout-image-print have weaker iOS justification.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Model-type palette (toolbar of model shapes) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift (AddModelSheet ~11426; availableModelTypes ~2813), src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm availableModelTypesForCreation (3963) | AddModelSheet lists 16 model types (Arches/CandyCanes/ChannelBlock/Circle/Cube/Custom/Icicles/Image/Matrix/MultiPoint/PolyLine/SingleLine/Sphere/Spinner/Star/Tree/WindowFrame). Tap a type then tap canvas to place. Wreath deliberately excluded (deprecated). Label model type is the only desktop palette shape not offered; DMX is a separate gap (see below). |
| Click/drag model placement (bounding-rect create) | Implemented | P0 | M | src-iPad/Metal/XLMetalBridge.h createModelOfType: (366), LayoutEditorView.swift canvas-tap create flow | After arming a type, tap on the Metal canvas creates a default model via ModelManager::CreateDefaultModel and places it; drag/resize handles follow. Touch idiom replaces desktop click-drag bounding rect. |
| Poly Line multi-point placement | Implemented | P1 | M | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift (layoutPolylineInProgress ~2586, Esc/Return commit ~566/3447), XLMetalBridge polyline vertex append | Polyline create is a multi-tap mode with Cancel/Done toolbar swap and Esc/Return hotkeys (hardware keyboard). Verified mid-polyline state handling exists. |
| Add 3D Object popup (Image, Gridlines, Terrain, Mesh, Ruler) | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift createViewObject ~325, perTypeBody ~10846; Bridge availableViewObjectTypes (5053)/createViewObjectWithType (5065) | View objects created via the ViewObjects sidebar tab rather than a model-palette popup, but covers all five desktop types (Image/Mesh/Gridlines/Terrain/Ruler, Ruler gated to one) with full per-type property editors and terrain heightmap brush. Equivalent capability, different entry point. |
| Add DMX model popup (General, Floodlight, Area Flood, Moving Head, Moving Head Adv, Servo, Servo 3D, Skull) | Missing | P1 | M | — | DMX fixture types are NOT in availableModelTypesForCreation (XLSequenceDocument.mm:3963). All DMX model classes exist in shared src-core/models/DMX/ and render fine on iPad, and createModelOfType: just forwards a type tag to ModelManager::CreateDefaultModel, so wiring is small: add the DMX type tags + a submenu in AddModelSheet. Existing DMX models load/edit/render today (the property editor already has extensive DMX-side rows); only NEW DMX-model creation is missing. |

| Model tree (hierarchical Model/Group list) | Partial | P1 | M | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift sidebar ~854/930 (Models/Groups/ViewObjects/Controllers tabs) | iPad uses four separate flat, filterable, sortable sidebar rosters (Models / Groups / ViewObjects / Controllers) instead of one unified hierarchical tree with nested groups/submodels/strands/nodes. Group membership and submodels are edited from the property pane, not by expanding tree nodes. Functionally covers navigation/selection but does not replicate the desktop's single expandable tree with in-line group/submodel nesting. |

| Preview background image & display options (property grid) | Partial | P2 | M | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift '2D Background' pseudo-object (handleBackgroundImagePick 412-421, perTypeBody not for bg), 2D grid/bbox toggles in PreviewSettings (15-16) | 2D background IMAGE is settable via a synthetic '2D Background' pseudo-object (J-8). 2D grid + bounding box + grid spacing surface via PreviewSettings overlays. | Save / Print / Save-as-image Layout | Missing | P3 | M | — | No Save-Layout-Image (PNG) or Print-Layout for the layout preview (PreviewPaneView exports image only for House/Model/Submodel previews per the capability map, not the layout editor). Printing is a weak iPad need; PNG export could reuse the MTKView capture path. Low priority. |
| Viewpoints / saved cameras (2D & 3D) | Implemented | P2 | S | src-iPad/Metal/XLMetalBridge.h viewpointNamesForDocument:/applyViewpointNamed:/saveCurrentViewAs:/deleteViewpointNamed:/restoreDefaultViewpointForDocument: (63-70) | Save/apply/delete named viewpoints and restore default; filtered to 2D/3D per pane. Matches desktop viewpoint_mgr. |
| Make Start Channel(s) Valid / Not Overlapping | Missing | P2 | S | — | No 'make start channels valid / not overlapping' fixer found (recalcModelStartChannels is internal on rename/delete but not a user-invokable repair across all models). Core rework-start-channels logic is shared; small bridge method + menu item. Useful when channel assignments get invalid/overlapping. |
| Unlink model/group from base show folder | Missing | P3 | S | — | Controller unlink-from-base exists (unlinkControllerFromBase:), but no equivalent for models/groups (desktop UnlinkSelectedModels). isFromBase is exposed in summaries so the UI knows; a bridge method clearing the FromBase flag + a menu item would close it. Low value. |
| Models vs 3D Objects tab toggle | Implemented | P2 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift LayoutSidebarTab (Models/Groups/ViewObjects/Controllers) sidebarTab picker (885) | Sidebar tab picker switches edit target between Models and ViewObjects (plus Groups/Controllers), superset of desktop's Models/3D-Objects notebook. |
| Direct preview selection & multi-select (click / shift / marquee) | Implemented | P0 | M | src-iPad/Metal/XLMetalBridge.h pickModel/pickModelsInRect (marquee)/pickViewObject, LayoutEditorView selection + MultiSelectActionBar | Tap-select, two-finger marquee multi-select (with 3D depth cutoff), selection rings/tints, sidebar<->canvas sync. Drives align/distribute/match/flip/group/bulk-edit. 3D pick has documented 2D-only limits in some paths. |
| Sequencer Views & Models panel: View management | Partial | P2 | M | src-iPad/App/DisplayElementsSheet.swift (addView/renameView/cloneView/moveViewUp/Down/deleteView 195-663), Bridge addView/deleteView/renameView/cloneView/moveView* | Add/Rename/Clone/Delete/Reorder views and Master view present. MISSING vs desktop: Copy-To-Master (make a user view the master), Import a view from a layout file, and Import master view from a sequence. Those import/master-promote operations are the gap. |
| Sequencer Views & Models panel: model membership & ordering | Partial | P2 | M | src-iPad/App/DisplayElementsSheet.swift two-pane add/remove + visibility (262-385), Bridge addModel:toViewAtIndex:/removeModel:fromViewAtIndex:/moveModel:inViewAtIndex: | Two-list add/remove/reorder + visibility toggles + filter implemented, plus remove-from-Master effect-loss warning. MISSING: the desktop right-click sort submenu (sort by name/controller-port/start-channel/type, groups-at-top, bubble-up groups) and the Hide-All/Hide-Unused/Show-All/Select-Unused-Used-All bulk operations. Membership editing is fully there; the convenience sort/bulk menu is the gap. |

## 7. Layout: Model Types & Properties

_Parity summary._ iPad parity in this area is remarkably high — the layout editor (LayoutEditorView.swift, 12.4k lines) and its bridge (perTypePropertiesForModel/setPerTypeProperty plus ~30 per-type Build*Props functions in XLSequenceDocument.mm) cover nearly the entire desktop ModelPropertyAdapter surface: per-type geometry for all model families (including all 8 DMX subtypes), the full common-property stack (structured start-channel editor, controller assignment, individual start channels, model chain, shadow model, string type / single+superstring colors, RGBW, appearance, low-def factor, aliases, strand/node names), the complete controller-connection section (port/protocol/speed, smart remote, every per-port override), and boxed/two-point/three-point/poly-point screen-location editing. The biggest remaining gaps are richness rather than presence: the Faces/States/Dimming editors are generic key→value attribute editors with no visual node-picker (NodeSelectGrid) or model-preview node mapping, and the Custom Model grid editor lacks the desktop dialog's transforms (flip/rotate/wire/compress/trim), cut/copy/paste, auto-numbering, and create-submodels-from-row/col/layer. New-model creation excludes DMX and Wreath types, and the Generate-Custom-Model video/photo wizard is absent (partly substituted by the iPad-only ARKit Map-from-Lights scan).

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Model creation palette (per-type buttons) | Partial | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift AddModelSheet (~11426), availableModelTypes (~2813); src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm availableModelTypesForCreation (3963) | AddModelSheet offers 17 of the desktop types (Arches, Candy Canes, Channel Block, Circle, Cube, Custom, Icicles, Image, Matrix, MultiPoint, Poly Line, Single Line, Sphere, Spinner, Star, Tree, Window Frame) plus vendor Download (VendorBrowserSheet) and .xmodel Import. Deliberately MISSING from the picker: DMX (no way to create any DMX model on iPad, though existing DMX models are fully editable) and Wreath (intentionally gated as deprecated). 'Add Object' (view objects) handled separately. To add DMX creation just expand the curated list + factory mapping; the per-type DMX property editors already exist. |

| Node Select Grid (node-range picker) | Missing | P1 | L | — | No NodeSelectGrid equivalent on iPad — the shared grid dialog desktop uses for faces/states/submodels/effects node selection (select all/none/invert, ordered selection, model-layout background, brightness, zoom, output-to-lights, cut/copy/paste). Its absence is WHY Faces/States editing degrades to a raw attribute editor. Building a touch NodeSelectGrid (it can reuse the custom-grid Canvas rendering and the iPadModelPreview node hit-testing already present) would lift Faces/States/SubModels to near-parity, hence P1. |

## 8. Layout: Submodels / Faces / States / Aliases

_Parity summary._ SubModels are the strongest part of this area on iPad: there's a full editor (add/copy/rename/delete/reorder, per-line ranges grid, vertical orientation, buffer style, sub-buffer rectangle editor, Generate Slices wizard, reverse/sort row ops, node-chase animation playback, aliases, and crucially an interactive Metal preview with tap-toggle + two-finger marquee node selection). Faces and States, by contrast, share a single generic flat key/value attribute editor (FaceStateEditorSheet) that exposes the raw FaceStateData map but has NO structured phoneme/eyes grid, NO Single-Node/Node-Range/Matrix type awareness, NO image picker, NO per-element color picker, and NO live preview/node selection — so they are usable for editing pre-existing definitions but far from desktop parity for authoring. Model and submodel Aliases editors are fully implemented. Import/export (from Model/File/CSV/Downloads/State/Face), output-to-lights live test, matrix face image download, and the Channel/Node Layout report are entirely absent across all three editors. The shared src-core (Model::SetFaceInfo/SetStateInfo/SubModel and the wx-free node-range/preview machinery) already backs everything, so most remaining gaps are SwiftUI-layer work rather than core work.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| SubModels editor dialog (entry + list management) | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift (SubModelListSheet ~5597; addSubModel 3056, renameSubModel 3117, deleteSubModel 3247, copySubmodel 5681) | Add (text field), delete (swipe), copy (swipe action, auto 'Copy N' naming), rename (inline in detail editor), and reorder (onMove on the per-line list) are present. List-level search/filter is the only missing piece vs desktop's OnButton_SearchClick; not load-bearing for typical submodel counts. |
| SubModel Node Ranges editor (per-strand grid) | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift SubModelDetailEditor.rangesSection (~6171), addRange/deleteActiveRow/moveActiveRow (6330+) | Per-line comma-separated range editing with add/delete/reorder lines, active-line selection, and live preview highlight via SubModelRangeOps.expand. Desktop's live Node Count / Line Count columns are not shown numerically but the count appears in the list row; effectively complete. |
| SubModel SubBuffer mode | Implemented | P2 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift SubBufferRectEditor (~6608); type Picker in editorForm (6042) | Segmented Ranges/Sub-buffer type picker plus a draggable corner/body rectangle editor in 0..100 buffer space, serialized to x1,y1,x2,y2 with a text mirror. Matches desktop SubBufferPanel intent. |
| SubModel buffer style + vertical layout option | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift editorForm Buffer Style picker (6050) + Vertical toggle (6049); bufferStyles list 5909 | Vertical-orientation toggle is wired. Buffer Style picker offers a hardcoded 8-entry subset ('Default','Keep XY','Stacked',...). Desktop pulls the full authoritative list from SubModel::GetBufferStyles (which can vary by model type); iPad should call that core method via the bridge instead of a static array to avoid drift/missing styles. |
| SubModel interactive node selection in 3D model preview | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/SubmodelPreviewPane.swift (handleTap nodeNearPoint 210, handleMarquee nodes(in:) 227); LayoutEditorView.swift toggleNode 6383 / addNodes 6401 | Tap-toggle assigns/removes a node to the active line; two-finger long-press marquee unions enclosed nodes into the active line; pinch/pan/double-tap navigate. Highlights the active line's nodes. Strong parity; preview is 2D pick (consistent with iPad's documented 3D-pick limitation). |
| SubModel 'Draw Model' / per-row node-select grid dialog | Partial | P3 | M | src-iPad/App/SubmodelPreviewPane.swift (interactive preview substitutes for the grid) | Desktop's flat NodeSelectGrid (a 2D matrix of the parent's physical layout for click-painting) is not ported. The interactive Metal preview covers the same 'paint nodes by tapping' use case more naturally on touch, so a separate grid dialog is low value; mark partial because the exact grid-paint affordance (whole-submodel paint via one dialog) is absent. |

| SubModel Action menu: flip/shift/reverse all | Missing | P2 | M | — | Bulk cross-submodel ops (Flip All Vertical/Horizontal, Shift All Nodes in All SubModels, Reverse All Nodes in All SubModels, Shift Nodes in selected submodel by offset with wrap) are not exposed. Per-submodel reverse exists; the all-submodels flips/shifts (desktop FlipVertical:4320, Shift:4211, ShiftSingleSubmodel:4254) need new bridge wrappers or Swift-side strand math + commit. |
| SubModel node-grid cleanup operations (duplicates/uniform/pivot) | Missing | P3 | L | — | Remove/Suppress Duplicates, Uniform Row Length, Pivot Rows/Columns, Combine/Expand/Compress strands, Convert Blanks/Zeros are all absent. These are power-user matrix cleanup tools; lots of surface (desktop RemoveDuplicates/MakeRowsUniform/PivotRowsColumns/CombineStrands). Mostly Swift-side strand-array transforms but many distinct ops. |
| SubModel geometric point sorting / Symmetrize | Missing | P3 | M | — | Geometric (spatial) point sorting and rotational Symmetrize (custom models only) are not ported. iPad only has numeric sort. Geometric sort/symmetrize need node XY positions, which the bridge can supply, but the dialog + math are unbuilt. |
| SubModel list operations: join / split / sort by name | Missing | P2 | M | — | No Sort by Name, Join, Join Single Strand, or Split. Sort-by-name is trivial Swift; Join/Split need strand-merge/partition logic (desktop JoinSelectedModels:4725, SplitSelectedSubmodel:4771) operating on the SubModelEntry list before commitDetails. |
| SubModel import: from Model / File / Layout / Downloads / CSV | Missing | P2 | L | — | No submodel import path at all. | SubModel import from State / Face definitions | Missing | P3 | M | — | Creating a submodel from an existing NodeRange State or Face (CreateSubmodel:3768) is not exposed. Since faceInfo/stateInfo are already readable via the bridge, this is mostly a Swift picker + node-union + addSubModel commit. |
| SubModel 'Import Custom Model Overlay' (matrix only) | Missing | P3 | XL | — | Overlaying a custom .xmodel onto a matrix to generate submodels/faces/states (ImportCustomModel:3790) is unported. Niche, complex alignment-offset workflow; low value on iPad. |
| SubModel export: CSV / xModel / to other models | Missing | P3 | M | — | No submodel export (CSV, .xmodel, or copy-to-other-models). Core has ExportSubModels/ExportSubModelAsxModel/ExportSubmodelToOtherModels; needs bridge wrappers + a fileExporter / model-multiselect sheet. |
| SubModel node animation playback | Implemented | P3 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift SubModelDetailEditor playControls (6001), startPlayback/advancePlayback (6293+), animationNodeSequence (5944) | In-editor node chase with adjustable Speed (1..10) and Trail (1..20) length, driving the embedded preview highlight. ## 9. Layout: DMX / Moving Heads / 3D Objects

_Parity summary._ iPad parity in this area is surprisingly strong for EDITING but has a clear hole in CREATION. Every DMX model type and every view-object type can be fully edited on iPad through the descriptor-driven per-type property panel (XLSequenceDocument.mm Build*Props at lines 6074-6816 + setPerTypeProperty), including color ability (RGBW/CMYW/Color Wheel), pan/tilt motors, beam/shutter/dimmer, presets, position zones, servo knobs, servo3d linkages, and skull servos — and these render through the shared src-core DMX/mesh draw path. The two structural gaps are: (1) you cannot CREATE a DMX model from the Add Model picker (availableModelTypesForCreation omits all DMX types, though createModelOfType/CreateDefaultModel already supports them in core — a near-trivial wiring fix), and (2) GDTF/LOR-prop import is absent (UTTypes are declared but the import path is generic pugixml-only). Remaining gaps are detail-level: per-mesh and per-servo-image transform sub-properties (offset/scale/rotate/brightness/mesh-only), PWM per-channel brightness/gamma, and view-object align/distribute/unlink-from-base.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Add DMX model (type picker) | Missing | P1 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm:3963 availableModelTypesForCreation (DMX types omitted); src-iPad/Metal/XLMetalBridge.mm:2172 createModelOfType already calls ModelManager::CreateDefaultModel | availableModelTypesForCreation returns only non-DMX types (Arches..Window Frame). createModelOfType -> CreateDefaultModel already supports 'Dmx*'/'Moving Head'/'Servo'/'Skull'/'Floodlight' in shared core, so adding the strings to the picker (plus a friendly-label mapping and a 3D-only gate for Servo 3D matching desktop) lights up creation. Editing of created/imported DMX models is already fully wired. Small effort because core CreateDefaultModel + all per-type editors already exist. |
| DMX # Channels (channel count) | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm DmxChannelCount prop emitted by every Build*Props (e.g. 6188, 6312, 6421, 6574, 6704, 6724); setPerTypeProperty handles it via UpdateChannelCount | MakeIntProp '# Channels' 1-512 present on Floodlight/MovingHead/MovingHeadAdv/General/Skull/Servo/Servo3d. Triggers core recalculation through setPerTypeProperty -> Reinitialize. |

| Import DMX model from xmodel / LOR prop | Partial | P2 | M | src-iPad/Metal/XLMetalBridge.mm:2243 importXModel via CreateDefaultModelFromSavedModelNode; src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift:305 declares lff/lpf UTTypes | xmodel import fully restores DMX/servo/mesh settings via the shared CreateDefaultModelFromSavedModelNode path and re-homes the start channel (NO_CONTROLLER). However the declared .lff/.lpf (LOR prop) UTTypes have NO LOR-specific parser on iPad — the generic pugixml load will fail for those formats. Need to wire the LOR import branch (desktop has it). xmodel side is done; LOR side missing. |
| View Object: Image | Implemented | P2 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm:4979 image VO summary (imageFile/brightness/transparency/scaleXYZ) + :5263 setter; createViewObjectWithType 'Image' :5065 | Create, edit (image file, transparency, brightness, scale), rename, duplicate, delete all wired. Renders via shared ImageObject::Draw. |
| View Object: Mesh (3D OBJ) | Implemented | P2 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm:4961 mesh VO summary (objFile/brightness/meshOnly/scaleXYZ) + setter; create 'Mesh' | Create + edit (OBJ file, brightness, mesh-only, scale) wired; renders via shared MeshObject::Draw / xlMesh. Material-filename-with-spaces fixup is desktop-side logic in MeshObject but core is shared so it applies. |
| View Object: Gridlines | Implemented | P3 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm:4994 gridlines VO summary (spacing/width/height/color/hasAxis/pointToFront) + setter; create 'Gridlines' | All gridlines properties present and editable. Real-world Grid Spacing readout (when a Ruler exists) not separately verified but core-derived. |
| View Object: Terrain | Implemented | P3 | M | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm:5008 terrain VO summary + setter; src-iPad/Metal/XLMetalBridge.h:184 editTerrainHeight; UI src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift:10917 terrainEditControls (raise/lower + brush delta) | Image/transparency/brightness, spacing, width/depth, grid color, hide-grid/hide-image, and an Edit-Terrain raise/lower brush sculpt mode are all wired through editTerrainHeight + heightmap undo snapshots. |

MISSING the 'Unlink Models/Objects from Base Show Folder' context action (no unlinkViewObject in iPad). Read-only display for base-folder objects only partially enforced. Small additive gap. |
| View Object align / distribute / flip / resize | Missing | P3 | M | src-iPad/Metal/XLMetalBridge.h:508 alignModels/:519 distributeModels/:528 matchSizeOfModels/:540 flipModels operate on MODEL names; MultiSelectActionBar (LayoutEditorView.swift:11782) targets the model selection | Multi-object align/distribute/flip/match-size exist for MODELS (which includes DMX models since they share BoxedScreenLocation), but there is no equivalent for VIEW OBJECTS — desktop's ViewObjectPanel has a separate PreviewObjectAlign*/Distribute*/Flip*/Resize set. iPad view-object multi-select with these ops is not wired. Core ScreenLocation transforms are shared so it's mostly mirroring the model bridge methods onto VO names. |
| DMX model 3D placement / transform (BoxedScreenLocation) | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/Metal/XLMetalBridge.h (drag/scale/rotate/handles + pickModel) and 2D/3D toggle src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift:12282; setLayoutModelProperty center/size/rotation in XLSequenceDocument.mm | DMX models use the same BoxedScreenLocation as other models, so move/rotate/scale on the layout canvas in both 2D and 3D (toggle present) works through the shared transform + handles::DragSession pipeline. Effects then drive DMX channels via the shared render path. Note: several bridge hit-test/handle methods return early in 3D (3D gizmo work is partial), which is a general layout-editor limitation, not DMX-specific. |

## 10. Layout: Preview, Background & View Objects

_Parity summary._ iPad parity in this area is unexpectedly strong: the entire preview/layout subsystem (the 542KB LayoutEditorView.swift plus the ~148KB XLMetalBridge.mm) drives the same shared src-core/ Model/ViewObject/ModelPreview/ViewpointMgr code as desktop, so 2D+3D preview, camera pan/zoom/orbit, fit/reset, named viewpoints (save/load/delete/restore-default, persisted to rgbeffects.xml), background image editing (image/brightness/alpha/scale-to-fit), grid/bbox/first-pixel/model-name/info overlays, active-preview selection with All Models/Unassigned pseudo-groups, model+view-object property editing, on-canvas handles, the 3D axis-tool gizmo, all five view-object types (Gridlines/Ruler/Image/Mesh/Terrain incl. paintable heightfield brush), and align/distribute/match/flip are all present and verified. The capability map's claim that "background editing is desktop-only" is stale — it is editable on iPad (LayoutEditorBackgroundPropertiesView). The genuine gaps are mostly long-tail: rename/delete of a named preview, group-center crosshair, full wiring-diagram view, real-world ruler-calibrated dimension readouts in the property pane, node hover tooltip, DXF export, and floating per-preview windows. Truly out-of-scope items are narrow: SpaceMouse 6-DOF (no 3Dconnexion driver on iPadOS) and direct printer output for the layout image (iOS shares an image instead).

## 11. Sequencer: Grid & Effect Editing

_Parity summary._ The iPad sequencer grid is at high parity for everyday effect editing: tap/marquee select, drag-move, edge-resize, shared-edge resize, fade-handle drag, palette-tap/double-tap create, a rich long-press context menu (align suite, close-gap, lock/disable/reset/randomize/description/preset/split/edit-timing/select-in-row/model/column), cut/copy/paste with cross-pasteboard sync, duplicate, delete, layer insert/delete/rename, row/model bulk copy/cut/paste/delete, undo/redo, zoom/scroll, and grouped keyboard nudge/stretch/extend/navigate commands — almost all wired to the shared src-core paths. The notable parity gaps are the AC (Absolute Cascade) draw mode (entirely absent), convert-to-different-effect-type, Create Random Effects across a cell range, the Duplicate-N-times-with-gap dialog, paste-by-cell vs paste-by-time, paste-as-layers, and keyboard "move effect up/down a layer" (the touch equivalent is cross-row drag). Several desktop pieces are touch idiom substitutions (palette-arm-then-tap instead of drag-from-dropper; play-marker split instead of right-click-point split) and a couple (hover status bar/tooltip) are genuinely out of scope on touch. Most missing items are pure SwiftUI+bridge wiring over already-shared core logic, so effort is mostly small-to-medium.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|

| Effect status / hover tooltip | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: Touch UI has no hover/cursor state or status bar; desktop hover tooltips and cursor-zone feedback don't translate to a finger-driven grid. — Hover-driven status-bar text and cursor-shape changes have no equivalent on a touch device (no persistent pointer/hover, no status bar). A trackpad-connected iPad could surface limited hover, but this is fundamentally a pointer-hover idiom. |

## 12. Sequencer: Timing Tracks & Waveform

_Parity summary._ iPad has strong parity here: the Metal-backed top-chrome waveform (peak+RMS), zoom/scroll/play-marker, all band/stem/vocal filters, onset/pitch/spectrogram overlays, sound classification, HTDemucs stems, and the full lyric/breakdown/auto-label/subdivide/create-from-effects pipeline are all wired through the shared src-core media + lyrics code (the desktop and iPad both link the same AudioManager, OnsetDetector, StemSeparator, PhonemeDictionary, etc.). The biggest real gaps are authoring-flow conveniences that desktop has but iPad doesn't surface yet: VAMP beat/bar/key analysis, Import Notes (Audacity/MusicXML/MIDI/Polyphonic), the broad multi-format timing-import dispatcher (iPad only exposes .xtiming in its file picker even though LOR/Papagayo bridge methods exist), arbitrary fixed-interval entry (CustomTimingDialog), Divide-by-N (only 2-way Halve exists), draggable waveform region-selection with Render-Selected-Region, granular remove-words/remove-phonemes, .pgo export, the phoneme user-dictionary editor, and Generate-Lyrics-From-Data. None of these is platform-blocked; they are mostly SwiftUI/bridge wiring on top of already-shared core. A handful of features (Ctrl-drag scrub, classify) are present in iPad-touch form. Overall this area is roughly 70-75% to parity with the remaining work being medium-effort UI/bridge additions.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|

Matches desktop Waveform::DrawWaveView. Fully wired via shared AudioManager GetLeftDataMinMax. |

| VAMP plugin beat/bar/key audio analysis | Missing | P2 | L | — | No VAMP/Queen Mary plugin support on iPad. The shared xLightsVamp lives in src-core/media but the VAMP plugins are external dynamic libraries that cannot be loaded under iOS App Store policy (same constraint that disables AI plugin DLLs). iPad already offers on-device tempo/chord/onset detection via Apple frameworks that cover much of VAMP's beat/key use, so this is a real platform constraint for the plugin-host mechanism but the analyses themselves are largely substituted. Treat as missing rather than out-of-scope only because a curated bundled-plugin or pure-core analyzer path could be built; the dynamic-plugin loading itself is App-Store-blocked. |
| Download VAMP plugins prompt | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: VAMP plugins are downloadable external dynamic libraries; loading third-party native code at runtime is prohibited by iOS App Store policy (same reason AI plugin dylib loading is disabled on iOS). The download prompt has no purpose without a loadable-plugin host. — Pointless on iPad without a runtime native-plugin host (App Store policy blocks loading downloaded dylibs). iPad substitutes the relevant analyses with on-device Apple-framework tempo/chord/onset detection, so there is nothing to download/prompt for. |

## 13. Sequencer: Rows / Display Elements / Views

_Parity summary._ iPad parity in this area is strong: the row header (RowHeaderViews.swift), the grid-area menu (SequencerGridV2View.swift), the Add Timing Track sheet, and the Display Elements editor (DisplayElementsSheet.swift) collectively cover the majority of high-value desktop row/timing/view operations, and the shared src-core SequenceElements/SequenceViewManager means most remaining gaps are pure SwiftUI/bridge wiring rather than new core logic. The biggest functional gaps are in the Display Elements editor (no sort strategies, bulk visibility helpers, select-used/unused, Make Master, import-view, panel-local undo, move-to-top/bottom) and in row-menu effect-scope operations (delete-by-scope beyond Row, Select Timing Marks, Copy Layers/SubModels to Models, Play Model, Show All Effects, Convert-data-to-effects, Import Notes). A handful of cosmetic heading indicators (tag-color chip, group icon, single-color swatch, grid-spacing preference) and a few niche generators (VAMP, full raw/rendered model export) are missing or out-of-scope. None of the gaps block a usable sequencer; they are incremental polish.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Row select + model-preview link | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/RowHeaderViews.swift (onSelect/onTapGesture, lines 91/134/274); SequencerViewModel selection drives preview | Tap on a row selects it and feeds the Metal model/house preview via setModelColors path; matches EVT_MODEL_SELECTED behavior. |
