## 14. Effects: All 55 Effect Panels & Rendering

_Parity summary._ iPad effect parity is high. The entire JSON-driven panel framework, all ~46 custom compound rows, visibility-rules engine, value curves, color/buffer/blending panels, and the render engine are ported or shared (every effect renders through the same src-core RenderableEffect/RenderEngine via iPadRenderContext, and effectmetadata JSON is loaded into RenderableEffect by the shared EffectManager). The dominant remaining gaps are NOT missing effects but missing code-driven dynamic UI behavior that desktop implements in C++ ValidateWindow() and which is absent from the JSON visibility rules: the VU Meter ~60-type IsType enable matrix, Text source-priority + To-Center/No-Repeat enables, Adjust action-dependent spin labels/enables, Piano/VUMeter MIDI note-order enforcement, plus a few un-populated code-driven choices (audio-track lists, Text lyric-track). Secondary gaps are the rich interactive Assist canvases (Pictures pixel-paint, Moving Head pan/tilt/dimmer/path) and convenience UI (animated preview thumbnails, Shader download, video-details popup, per-parameter lock).

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| JSON-driven effect panel framework | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/EffectSettingsView.swift, src-iPad/App/EffectPropertyView.swift, src-iPad/Metadata/EffectMetadata.swift, src-iPad/App/NotebookTabsView.swift, src-iPad/App/XYCenterPadView.swift, src-iPad/App/Point2DPropertyView.swift | Full re-implementation in SwiftUI of JsonEffectPanel: dispatches slider/checkbox/togglebutton/choice/combobox/spin/text/filepicker/fontpicker/point2d/custom; group layouts tabs/section/xyCenter. EffectMetadata.swift re-derives setting-key prefixes line-for-line with JsonEffectPanel.cpp. Same 56 effectmetadata JSON files consumed. No work needed. |
| Effect panel registration / metadata caching | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/iPadRenderContext.cpp:62 (EffectManager(...+"/effectmetadata")); shared src-core/effects/EffectManager.cpp:269 SetMetadata; src-core/effects/RenderableEffect.cpp Get*Default helpers | Shared core: iPadRenderContext constructs EffectManager with the resources/effectmetadata dir, so SetMetadata caches JSON onto each RenderableEffect exactly as desktop. Render() reads cached defaults/min/max identically. iPad parses+caches per-effect metadata in SequencerViewModel.metadataCache for the UI side. |
| Visibility rules engine (conditional enable/show) | Partial | P1 | M | src-iPad/Metadata/EffectMetadata.swift:154 (VisibilityRuleMetadata), src-iPad/App/EffectSettingsView.swift:721-799 (evaluateCondition: equals/notEquals/oneOf/notOneOf/greaterThan/startsWith) | The declarative rule engine is fully ported and evaluated. The gap is upstream/data: many desktop effects (VUMeter, Text, Adjust, Faces partially) implement their dynamic enable/show/label logic in C++ ValidateWindow() rather than in JSON visibilityRules, so those JSONs carry zero rules and iPad shows all controls always enabled. Closing this means either authoring the missing rules into the shared JSON (benefits both platforms) or replicating the per-effect logic; see VUMeter/Text/Adjust/Piano entries. |

Gaps: (1) the From-Lyrics timing-track source — Text_LyricTrack choice has no dynamicOptions, so it renders empty (needs lyricTimingTracks dynamicOptions in JSON, trivial+shared); (2) source-priority resolution (Text vs File vs Lyrics) and the To-Center/No-Repeat enable-when-direction!=none logic are desktop ValidateWindow code with no JSON visibility rules — author rules or replicate. Render is shared. |
| Sketch effect (rich custom panel + Assist canvas) | Implemented | P2 | S | shared src-core/effects/SketchEffect.cpp; Sketch.json; custom rows Sketch_Info/Sketch_DefRow/Sketch_PathEditor/Sketch_BackgroundRow -> SketchInfoRowView, SketchDefRowView, SketchPathEditorRowView (src-iPad/App/SketchPathEditorRowView.swift, 483 lines), SketchBackgroundRowView | The Assist sketch-tracing canvas is fully reimagined as the in-panel SketchPathEditorRowView touch editor, plus background-image row with opacity, info block, and read-only def string. Shared render (SketchEffectDrawing). At parity, arguably better as a touch idiom. |
| Shader effect (rich custom panel, GLSL/ISF) | Partial | P2 | M | shared src-core/effects/ShaderEffect.cpp (USE_GLES/ANGLE on iPad); Shader.json; custom rows Shader_FilenameBlock, Shader_SpeedRow -> ShaderSpeedRowView, Shader_DynamicParams -> ShaderDynamicParamsView (parses .fs uniforms via shaderDynamicPropertiesJsonForPath) | Shader runs on iPad via ANGLE/GLES 3.0 on Metal; file select, Clear, speed+lead-in, and the dynamically-generated uniform controls (ShaderConfig-driven, same JSON property array as desktop) are ported. Gaps: (1) the Download button (ShaderDownloadDialog to fetch shaders) is absent; (2) the animated GPU-rendered preview thumbnail in the panel is absent; (3) coordinate-shader X/Y-offset+zoom rows and auto-canvas-mode detection should be verified. Download/preview are convenience. |
| VU Meter effect (rich custom panel, ~60 audio modes) | Partial | P1 | L | shared src-core/effects/VUMeterEffect.cpp; VUMeter.json (16 plain props, 0 visibility rules, no custom rows); SVGFile filepicker present | Render shared and all 60 Type modes work. BUT the desktop VUMeterPanel ValidateWindow IsType matrix — which gates Bars/Gain(VC)/Sensitivity/Start+End-note/timing-track+regex/filter/X-Y-offset/logX/slow-down-falls/SVG per the ~60 Type values — is C++ code, NOT in the JSON, so on iPad every control is always visible/enabled (confusing, lets users set ignored params). Also missing: VUMeter_AudioTrack choice is empty (no audioTracks dynamicOptions), and start<=end note-order enforcement + note-name tooltips. Fix is substantial JSON authoring (large oneOf-based visibility ruleset) plus an audioTracks dynamicOptions source; the note-order/tooltips may need a small custom row. |
| Music effect (custom panel) | Partial | P2 | M | shared src-core/effects/MusicEffect.cpp; MusicEffect.json (0 visibility rules, no custom rows, no dynamicOptions) | VAMP-driven render is shared core and works. As with VUMeter, any code-driven enable logic and the note-range/audio-track population from desktop MusicPanel are not represented in JSON, so controls show statically. Audio-track choice (if present) would be empty without an audioTracks dynamicOptions source. Author visibility/dynamicOptions into MusicEffect.json (shared). |
| Moving Head effect (rich multi-tab DMX panel) | Partial | P2 | XL | shared src-core/effects/MovingHeadEffect.cpp; MovingHead.json; custom rows MHFixtures/MHIpadInfo/MHColorRow/MHDimmerRow/MHPathRow -> MovingHeadFixtureRowView (src-iPad/App/MovingHeadFixtureRowView.swift) etc. | iPad supports fixture selection (8 checkboxes), pan/tilt/offset/groupings/cycles, single-colour and constant dimmer-intensity authoring. EXPLICITLY NOT ported (code says 'still uses desktop's Effect Assist panel'): the interactive pan/tilt drag canvas, multi-segment dimmer-curve canvas, full waypoint path-drawing canvas, RGB color-wheel picker, the Status tab, and .xmh preset Save/Load. The MH beams still RENDER on iPad (shared DMX model code), but rich authoring is desktop-mostly. XL because it is essentially 4 interactive canvases + preset IO. |
| DMX effect (custom 48-channel panel) | Partial | P2 | M | shared src-core/effects/DMXEffect.cpp; DMX.json; custom rows DMX_ChannelsNotebook -> DMXChannelsNotebookView (48 sliders + invert, src-iPad/App/EffectCustomRowsFinal.swift:510) and DMX_ButtonsRow -> DMXButtonsRowView; bridge dmxSaveState/LoadState/RemapChannels | All 48 channel sliders + invert toggles are present (round-trips desktop sequences) and Save/Load State + a 6-preset Remap are wired. Missing vs desktop: (1) per-channel value-curve buttons (noted follow-up), (2) per-channel buddy text fields, (3) the full RemapDMXChannels grid editor (scale/offset/invert across selected effects) — iPad has only a 6-preset menu, and (4) Save-As-State is in-memory-only this session, NOT persisted to xlights_rgbeffects.xml (desktop-authored states load fine). Channel labels from model node names should be verified. |
| Servo effect (custom linked panel) | Implemented | P3 | S | shared src-core/effects/ServoEffect.cpp; Servo.json; custom rows Servo_StartEndRow -> ServoStartEndRowView, Servo_ButtonRow -> ServoButtonRowView; Channel modelNodeNames + Servo_TimingTrack lyricTimingTracks dynamicOptions | Start/End rows, Equal/Swap buttons, channel choice (model node names) and timing-track (phoneme) mode are ported. Verify the link-to-previous/next-Servo chaining buttons behave (ServoButtonRowView), but the panel and its dynamicOptions are present. Shared render. |
| Color / Palette panel (cross-cutting, every effect) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/ColorPaletteView.swift, ColorPanelCustomRows.swift, EffectPaletteView.swift, ColorCurveEditor.swift; custom rows PaletteHeaderRow/ChromaKeyRow/SparklesRow/BrightnessLevelRow; resources/effectmetadata/shared/Color.json | 8 swatch slots with enable checkboxes + per-slot color-curve, palette menu (Save/Save As/Load/Import-from-text/AI Generate), HSV (brightness/contrast/hue/sat/value, all VC-able), Sparkles, Chroma key, Brightness Level toggle all ported. Minor gaps: palette reverse / shift-left / shift-right buttons and the recent-palettes dropdown and algorithmic 'Generate' appear absent; the panel-reset preference is intentionally omitted on iPad (ResetPanelRow renders EmptyView). Functionally at parity. |
| Buffer panel (cross-cutting, every effect) | Implemented | P0 | S | resources/effectmetadata/shared/Buffer.json; custom rows SubBuffer -> SubBufferEditorView (interactive drag handles), RotoZoomPreset -> RotoZoomPresetRowView; render style/camera dynamicOptions | Render style, buffer stagger, per-preview camera (cameras dynamicOptions), transform, blur (VC), persistent, the interactive sub-buffer rectangle picker (SubBufferEditorView with corner/edge drag handles), and the Roto-Zoom preset row + Z/X/Y rotations/pivots/zoom are all ported. At parity. |
| Blending / Transitions panel (cross-cutting, every effect) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/BlendingPanelViews.swift; resources/effectmetadata/shared/Blending.json; custom rows LayerMorphRow/LayerMethodRow/CanvasRow/In_Transition_Header/Out_Transition_Header | Suppress/Freeze frames, Layer Morph + mix, Layer Method, Canvas mode + layer-select, and In/Out transition headers (type/fade/adjustment-VC/reverse with the enabled-only-when-fade>0 logic) are ported. | Value curves (animate any parameter over time) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/ValueCurveEditor.swift, ValueCurveCanvases.swift, ValueCurvePresetSheets.swift; bridge XLValueCurve over src-core/render/ValueCurve | Full type set (Ramp, Ramp Up/Down(+Hold), Parabolic, Logarithmic, Exponential, Sine/Abs/Decaying Sine, Square, Random, Custom hand-drawn, plus Music/Timing-track-driven), per-type parameter sliders, custom-point editing, presets save/load (.xvc), and per-property min/max/divisor + narrower VC ranges all ported. Round-trips through the shared ValueCurve core. At parity. (One unused-parameter slider renders as a disabled placeholder — cosmetic.) |
| Bulk edit (apply one setting to all selected effects) | Partial | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/PropertyContextMenu.swift (Apply to N Other Selected, Copy/Paste Value, Copy/Paste Value Curve); src-iPad/App/EffectSettingsView.swift (Update All / anchor-values multi-select chrome); SequencerViewModel.applyValueToAllSelected | iPad implements bulk edit via two paths: per-property long-press 'Apply to N Other Selected' and a top-bar 'Update All' that flushes the anchor effect's values to the selection. E_ keys are filtered per target. Gaps vs desktop: file-picker Filename/Path/Show-Folder bulk variants and the checkbox Checked/Unchecked variants are not offered as discrete menu items (a single value-apply covers most cases). Functionally close; small polish to add the file-picker variants. |
| Lock / unlock parameters (random-protection) | Missing | P3 | M | EffectMetadata.swift parses the 'lockable' field but no UI/state exists | The 'lockable' metadata flag is parsed but there is no lock toggle in the inspector and no per-setting lock-state tracking, so randomize (which exists on iPad) cannot be told to protect a parameter. Desktop tracks lock state by setting name via xlLockButton. Low value on iPad (random-effect generation is a niche workflow); would need a per-property lock toggle + a lock-set persisted with the effect. |
| Effect Assist panel (interactive canvases) | Partial | P2 | L | Morph -> MorphLineEditorRowView; Sketch -> SketchPathEditorRowView; (Pictures pixel-paint canvas absent) | iPad has no separate dockable Assist pane; instead it inlines touch editors per effect. | adjustSettings() effect-version migration | Implemented | P1 | S | shared src-core/effects/RenderableEffect.cpp (needToAdjustSettings/adjustSettings/CheckEffectSettings) + per-effect overrides; invoked on load through the shared SequenceElements/EffectManager path used by iPadRenderContext | Pure shared core. Sequences opened on iPad run the same migration on load (legacy buffer-style remaps, deprecation warnings). No iPad-specific work; behaves identically since iPad uses the same load path. |
| Settings serialization round-trip (legacy-key fidelity) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/Metadata/EffectMetadata.swift (re-derives E_/T_/B_/C_ + SLIDER_/TEXTCTRL_/CHOICE_/CHECKBOX_ prefixes matching JsonEffectPanel.cpp line-for-line; special cases like CHECKBOXBRIGHTNESSLEVEL, E_0FILEPICKERCTRL_IFS hard-coded in custom rows); shared SettingsMap serialization in core | Setting keys are produced identically to desktop, and custom rows reuse the exact legacy IDs (verified: Shader uses E_0FILEPICKERCTRL_IFS, Pictures uses E_TEXTCTRL_Pictures_Filename, etc.). The .xsq write path is shared core (SequenceFile). Older sequences round-trip unchanged on iPad. |
| Render cache hinting | Implemented | P3 | S | shared src-core/effects/RenderableEffect.cpp SupportsRenderCache; iPadRenderContext embeds RenderCache (src-iPad/Bridge/iPadRenderContext.h) | Pure shared core; iPadRenderContext owns a RenderCache and the RenderEngine consults SupportsRenderCache identically. No iPad work. |

## 15. Color, Palettes & Value Curves

_Parity summary._ The iPad has strong parity on the high-value core of this area: the 8-slot palette grid, per-swatch color editing, full ColorCurve editor (gradient + 9 spatial/temporal modes), and a complete Value Curve editor (all 23 types, custom points, reverse/flip, wrap, time offset, music/timing binding, .xvc presets, clipboard) are all wired through the shared src-core XLValueCurve/XLColorCurve wrappers, so curves round-trip byte-for-byte with desktop. Brightness/Contrast/HSV-adjust, Chroma Key, Sparkles (+music+color+VC), and Brightness Level are present via shared Color.json metadata. The notable gaps are the palette-manipulation toolbar buttons (reverse / shift / lock slots), the recent-palettes dropdown + recent-colors/CSS swatches, drag-and-drop onto swatches, sequence-wide color replace, and the color-dropper panel — most are quick SwiftUI/bridge additions since the underlying core ops already exist. Genuinely platform-different items are the custom HSV/RGB picker (iPad uses the native ColorPicker idiom) and Color Manager / dimming-curve preview canvas (low-value desktop-only chrome).

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| 8-slot palette color grid | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/ColorPaletteView.swift (paletteRow, C_CHECKBOX_Palette1..8 / C_BUTTON_Palette1..8) | Full 8-slot grid with per-slot enable toggle + color/curve binding. Reads/writes the same C_ keys as desktop GetColorString. Default-off matches Effect::ParseColorMap. |
| Palette color picker (per swatch) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/ColorPaletteView.swift (colorBinding + SwiftUI ColorPicker, sRGB-pinned hex round-trip) | Uses native SwiftUI ColorPicker per slot; serializes #RRGGBB via hexFromColor with explicit sRGB conversion to round-trip exactly. Functionally equivalent to desktop swatch click. |
| Custom HSV/RGB color picker dialog | Out-of-scope | P3 | L | src-iPad/App/ColorPaletteView.swift / ColorPanelCustomRows.swift (native SwiftUI ColorPicker used everywhere) | OUT-OF-SCOPE: iOS provides a rich native color picker (UIColorPickerViewController via SwiftUI ColorPicker) that is the platform-standard idiom; building a custom HSV-disc dialog would fight the OS and add no user value. — iPad uses the system ColorPicker (HSB grid, sliders, hex entry, eyedropper) for all color editing. Reimplementing xLights' bespoke xlColourPickerDialog (HSV disc, randomize, old/new preview, System Picker fallback) would duplicate native functionality and break the iOS interaction idiom. |

Pure local op, no render-core dependency. |

A Metal/Canvas preview drawing the gamma curve is feasible (shared graphics stack), but this is niche model-setup chrome. Low priority. |

## 16. Import / Export (sequences & data)

_Parity summary._ iPad has a solid core slice of this area: xLights .xsq/.xsqz effect import with a real channel-map tree + auto-map + .xmaphint hints, SuperStar (.sup) import, Package Sequence (.xsqz), vendor-model download, per-model FSEQ/.eseq export, and 3 of desktop's 10 timing-import formats — all driven by genuine src-core logic. The biggest gaps are: (1) the rich channel-map dialog features (save/load .xmap/.xjmap, AI map, find/filter, timeline preview, right-click menu, update-aliases, import-media options) that are wx-only today; (2) all 8 legacy/competitor sequence importers (LOR LMS/LPE/S5, HLS, Vixen2/3, LSP, VSA) whose parsers live in src-ui-wx and are not core-reusable; (3) the Export Effects CSV / Export Models XLSX reports and the batch Convert dialog. Several gaps are cheap wins because the work is already in src-core (e.g. 6 additional timing-import processors, SequencePackage, MusicXML/note import would need a parser port).

## 17. Media & Audio

_Parity summary._ Media & Audio is one of the stronger iPad parity areas. Because src-core/ (AudioManager, decoders, VideoReader, OnsetDetector/TempoDetector/ChordDetector, StemSeparator, SoundClassifier, SequenceMedia, RenderEngine) is shared, the iPad already has real audio playback transport, the full filtered/stem/analysis waveform stack, alternate-track CRUD, a Media tab (embed/extract/replace/rename/remove-unused), main-audio swap, and audio-driven timing-track generation (onsets/tempo/chords/AI-lyrics/LRCLIB) — most of it verified wired through XLSequenceDocument. The notable remaining gaps are workflow features that exist on desktop but lack iPad UI: adding new media into a sequence with the outside-folder placement/embed prompt, reload-from-disk, bulk-find-missing, AI-generate-into-media, animated/shader preview, plus the Sequence Video Preview panel and Jukebox. A few items are genuine platform constraints (audio output device enumeration on iOS, VAMP plugins which are desktop-only, and video transcode/encode which the bridge explicitly marks desktop-only).

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|

Missing vs desktop: an Add-media button, animated/shader-generated previews (still thumbnail only), Reload-from-disk, Bulk-find, AI-generate, and a dedicated action-button column. Grouping is by media type rather than desktop's source-directory + '(Embedded)' buckets. |

| Export rendered sequence as video | Out-of-scope | P3 | XL | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: GenericVideoExporter (src-ui-wx/media/VideoExporter) is a wx-UI desktop component and relies on the FFmpeg encode path that the iPad lib does not build (the bridge explicitly marks video transcode/encode desktop-only). Rendering+muxing video on-device would need an AVAssetWriter-based reimplementation; deferred and not a parity blocker for sequencing. — No VideoExporter on iPad; the bridge exposes no video-export method. |

## 18. Controllers: Upload Protocols

_Parity summary._ The iPad has surprisingly strong parity for the two most important upload workflows: single-controller Output/Input upload (full BaseController vendor dispatch, all vendor handlers compile from shared src-core) and FPP Connect (discovery, per-instance Cape/Models/UDP-Out/Proxies/Playlist config, parallel custom-FSEQ multi-target upload with progress/cancel/failed-upload reporting). All the heavy lifting — UDController validation, virtual-string generation, smart-remote tagging, every vendor handler, and FPP's full upload machinery — lives in wx-free src-core and is already wired through XLSequenceDocument.mm, so most gaps are missing SwiftUI affordances rather than missing capability. The notable genuine gaps are: the entire HinksPix Export dialog (SD-card HSEQ/AU/schedule authoring), the Bulk Controller Upload dialog, the FPP Connect user-facing FSEQ codec selector and Add-FPP/Re-Discover buttons, the XLSX controller-connection export, and auto-upload-on-output-enable. Nothing here is truly out-of-scope for iOS except FFmpeg-dependent media transcode edges — these are network HTTP uploads that iOS handles fine.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Upload Output config (single controller) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm:13001 uploadOutputForController: -> runUpload:input:NO (12913); src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift:1229 startControllerUpload, contextMenu Upload at 1823-1828 | Fully wired: RecalcStartChannels pre-flight, BaseController::CreateBaseController(c,ip), bc->SetOutputs(mm,om,c,cbs). Reached via Layout Editor Controllers tab long-press > Upload (gated to open-source-firmware rows). Result alert shows per-leg message + captured log. Only difference vs desktop is entry point (Layout Editor sidebar vs Setup tab button). |
| Upload Input (universe) config (single controller) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm:13005 uploadInputForController: -> runUpload:input:YES; gated by caps->SupportsInputOnlyUpload() (12934) | bc->SetInputUniverses(c,cbs) via shared core. Gating mirrors desktop. Surfaced through the same startControllerUpload path which runs input then output. |
| Linked input+output upload | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/LayoutEditorView.swift:1242-1264 startControllerUpload | iPad's single Upload action always runs both input (if SupportsInputOnlyUpload) and output (if SupportsUpload) in sequence — effectively always-linked. There is no separate unlinked toggle, but functionally this matches desktop's linked-upload behavior. No standalone 'IsControllerUploadLinked' preference. |

ZCPP/DDP-specific exceptions not separately modeled. |

Worth having because uploading 10-30 controllers one-at-a-time via long-press is tedious. |

## 19. Render Engine & FSEQ Export

_Parity summary._ iPad parity in this area is high. The iPad runs the exact same shared src-core RenderEngine, JobPool, RenderCache, RenderTree, SequenceData, PixelBuffer, and FSEQFile code as the desktop via iPadRenderContext (a real RenderContext subclass), so the entire effect render pipeline — render-all, incremental render-dirty, single-effect/range render, render-order dependency tree, model blending, and all per-layer render features (24 blending modes, transitions, brightness/contrast/HSV, sparkles, blur, rotozoom, buffer style/sub-buffer/stagger, canvas, chroma, freeze/suppress, brightness-level, color/palette/value-curve engine, dimming curves) is fully present and exercised through the SwiftUI Blending/Color/Buffer panels driven by shared effectmetadata JSON. FSEQ write (V2/zstd/sparse with FPP-command + media headers), render-on-save, save-FSEQ-on-save, FSEQ output folder config, FSEQ short-circuit load, eseq sub-sequence export, batch render, and per-model/per-effect render-disable are all wired. The real gaps are peripheral: no FSEQ version/compression preference (hardcoded V2/zstd/sparse), no multi-format export (LOR/Vixen/LSP/HLS/GIF/video — only FSEQ/eseq), no detailed per-model render-progress dialog or render-complete bell/status (only a spinner + fraction used in batch), no imported Data Layers (ISEQ), no GPU-render or render-cache-mode/size preferences, and no standalone fseq_convert tool.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Render All | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/iPadRenderContext.cpp:1767 RenderAll; src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h:1558 renderAll; src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift:2186 startBackgroundRender/beginFreshRender; toolbar src-iPad/App/SequencerView.swift:450; cmd src-iPad/App/XLightsCommands.swift:338 (Render All, Cmd-R) | Full re-render via shared RenderEngine.BuildRenderTree + Render. Runs on a background Thread with abort-then-restart chaining; toolbar button + Cmd-R match desktop. Renders the effect grid; ISEQ data-layers below/above are not run (no data layers on iPad). |
| Render-dirty (incremental render) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h:1541 renderEffectForRow; src-iPad/Bridge/iPadRenderContext.cpp:1743 RenderEffectForModel (delegates to shared RenderEngine.RenderEffectForModel); called after edits in SequencerViewModel | Edits trigger per-model range re-render through the same shared RenderEngine path the desktop uses (RenderEffectForModel honors persistent/downstream dependencies). The SwiftUI layer calls renderEffectForRow after batching setting changes rather than an implicit dirty-range sweep, but the underlying core dirty logic (Element::GetDirtyRange, downstream propagation) is the shared code. |
| Render single effect / model for a time range | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h:1541 renderEffectForRow:atIndex:; :1545 renderRangeForRow:startMS:endMS:clear:; iPadRenderContext.cpp:1743 RenderEffectForModel | Both single-effect render and arbitrary range render (with clear) are bridged and route to the shared RenderEngine. Used after drop/edit/delete to refresh output, mirroring desktop RenderUI entry points. |

The shared engine already supports a frame range, so wiring is light. |

Mirrors desktop OpenRenderAndSaveSequencesF (no 'exit when done' since the app stays open, which is the right iPad idiom). |

## 20. Preferences & Settings

_Parity summary._ iPad has NO unified Preferences editor — desktop's 10-page wxPreferencesEditor is replaced by a handful of scattered, purpose-specific sheets: FolderConfigView (show/media/fseq/base-show folders), SequenceSettingsSheet's Render tab (model-blend, frame rate, autosave), AIServicesSettingsSheet, and a few @AppStorage-backed view toggles in menus. The genuinely user-facing settings that matter for a sequencer (folders, fseq-on-save, AI services, autosave, snap-to-timing) are present, mostly implemented well. The large remaining gap is the breadth of granular preferences: ~40 desktop toggles/choices (effect-grid appearance, view options, render-on-save, render cache, backups, output sync, check-sequence suppression, color manager, video export, tip-of-the-day, etc.) are missing, hardcoded, or out-of-scope. Many missing items are low-value polish; the high-value gaps are render-on-save, paste-as mode, effect-grid spacing/appearance toggles, and a backup-on-save story.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Preferences dialog shell (multi-page editor) | Partial | P1 | M | src-iPad/App/FolderConfigView.swift, src-iPad/App/SequenceSettingsSheet.swift, src-iPad/App/AIServicesSettingsSheet.swift | No single unified Preferences editor. Settings are split across FolderConfigView (folders), SequenceSettingsSheet's Render tab, and AIServicesSettingsSheet, plus several @AppStorage view toggles buried in context menus. There is no top-level 'Preferences…' / 'Settings…' menu entry that gathers app-wide prefs. The right iPad idiom is a single Settings sheet (or iPad Settings.app bundle) collecting the app-global toggles; today they don't exist to collect. Effort is mostly the SwiftUI shell since most underlying state is per-feature. |
| Backup On Save | Missing | P2 | M | — | No backup-on-save on iPad. The bridge has no SetBackupOnSave/BackupOnSave (grep of XLSequenceDocument.h shows only writeAutosaveBackup for .xbkp recovery). iPad does autosave-recovery (.xbkp) but not a zipped show-folder backup. Desktop logic lives in src-ui-wx (BackupSettingsPanel + frame backup routines) which is not in shared core, so this needs both a core-able backup routine and SwiftUI wiring. Lower value on iPad given iCloud versioning, but a deliberate per-show backup is still useful. |
| Backup On Launch | Missing | P3 | M | — | Not present. Depends on the same backup machinery as Backup On Save (none exists on iPad). Marginal value on iPad; bundle with any backup-feature effort. |
| Backup Subfolders | Missing | P3 | S | — | Sub-option of the backup feature, which is absent entirely. Trivial once a backup feature exists. |
| Purge Backups interval | Missing | P3 | S | — | No backups, so no purge. Trivial follow-on to a backup feature. |
| Backup Directory (use show folder or custom) | Missing | P3 | M | — | No backup feature. A custom directory picker would reuse FolderConfigView's ShowFolderPicker + security-scoped bookmark pattern (FolderConfig.registerBookmark) if backups are added. |
| Alternative Backup Directory | Missing | P3 | M | — | No backup feature; even on desktop this is low-value. Skip unless backups land first. |
| Effect Icon Size | Partial | P3 | S | src-iPad/App/EffectsMetalGridView.swift | Not a user preference on iPad. The grid auto-buckets effect icons (16/24/32/48/64 px) by available row height (EffectsMetalGridView draws bucketed icons) rather than a fixed Small/Medium/Large/XL choice. There is no toolbar/dropper with a configurable icon size on iPad. Effectively superseded by the touch UI; expose as a pref only if users ask. |

It's always-on rather than a toggle, which matches the iPad idiom (overlay controls auto-fade). No persisted preference, but the user-visible capability exists. |
| Auto Show House Preview | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | src-iPad/App/SequencerView.swift | OUT-OF-SCOPE: iPad has no floating/auto-appearing House Preview window concept — the house preview is an embedded pane in SequencerView (or a detached scene the user explicitly opens). There is no auto-show-on-event behavior to toggle; window/scene management is governed by iPadOS scene lifecycle, not an app preference. |

Marginal even on desktop. |

Effort is a Settings control + plumbing GridMetrics through to the Metal grids (which already read it) and a ResizeMainSequencer-equivalent reload. |

Reachable from Tools -> AI Services…. Note AI plugin DLL/dylib loading is intentionally disabled on iOS (App Store policy) — only built-in services, which is the correct scope. |
| AI Service test connection | Implemented | P3 | S | src-iPad/App/AIServicesSettingsSheet.swift:224-327 | Implemented: the Test section picks an available/enabled service and runs testService (-> aiBase::TestLLM) on a background queue, reporting OK/Error inline. Matches desktop's ChoiceServicesTest + Test button. |
| Apply-immediately vs deferred apply semantics | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/App/AIServicesSettingsSheet.swift, src-iPad/App/SequenceSettingsSheet.swift, src-iPad/App/FolderConfigView.swift | iPad settings apply with mixed semantics by sheet: AIServicesSettingsSheet and SequenceSettingsSheet's Render tab write through immediately (matching macOS apply-immediately), while FolderConfigView uses an explicit Cancel/Done (deferred apply) because changing the show folder triggers a reload. There's no single consistent policy or a ShouldApplyChangesImmediately equivalent. Acceptable today, but as more prefs are added a unified convention (and likely apply-immediately for app-global toggles) should be chosen to avoid inconsistency. |

## 21. AI Features

_Parity summary._ iPad has strong AI parity at the core/service level: the shared src-core/ai ServiceManager, every built-in provider (Claude, ChatGPT, Gemini, Ollama, GenericClient, plus Apple Intelligence via the linked xLights-Apple-core lib), Keychain-backed secret storage, the Services config+Test panel, AI color-palette generation, AI image generation (embedded into the Pictures effect), and on-device AI speech-to-text lyric tracks are all wired and working through XLAIServices/XLAIImageSession. The notable gaps are all in the AI Image dialog's post-generation editing surface (no style-preset picker, no crop, no resize, no reset, no black-background flood-fill on save) and the entire AI model-mapping feature on sequence import (no AI Map button in ImportEffectsView; structured GenerateModelMapping exists in core but is unwired, and the prompt-file fallback lives in wx-only code). Plugin DLL loading is correctly out-of-scope (App Store policy), and the Media-Manager AI button plus the row-heading "AI Speech 2 Lyrics" entry are minor missing entry points (the lyric flow itself exists via the Add Timing Track sheet).

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| AI service architecture (ServiceManager + aiBase) | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLAIServices.mm (owns ServiceManager via XLiPadServiceSettingsStore), src-iPad/Bridge/XLAIServices.h | Full parity. XLAIServices.shared() constructs a real src-core ServiceManager with the iPad settings store; serviceManager/findService exposed to .mm callers; hasEnabledServiceForCapability maps the aiType TYPE set. Plugin dir passed as empty string by design. |
| Claude (Anthropic) provider | Implemented | P1 | S | shared src-core/ai/claude.cpp registered by ServiceManager; surfaced via src-iPad/Bridge/XLAIServices.mm allServices() | Provider is shared core code; registered automatically. Prompt/ColorPalette work end-to-end on iPad. Its MAPPING capability is registered but the iPad import UI never calls GenerateModelMapping (see AI model mapping gaps). |
| ChatGPT (OpenAI) provider | Implemented | P1 | S | shared src-core/ai/chatGPT.cpp + OpenAIAPI.cpp; surfaced via XLAIServices.mm | Color Palette + Prompt fully usable. OpenAIAPI image generation is reachable through XLAIImageSession when the service exposes IMAGES; speech-to-text transcription reachable via generateLyricTrack. |
| Google Gemini provider | Implemented | P2 | S | shared src-core/ai/gemini.cpp; surfaced via XLAIServices.mm; image via XLAIImageSession.mm | Prompt/ColorPalette work. Gemini's image generator is reachable through XLAIImageSession, but its style-preset property (GetProperties) is not rendered by the iPad image sheet (see Image generator style presets gap). |
| Ollama (local LLM) provider | Implemented | P3 | S | shared src-core/ai/ollama.cpp; surfaced via XLAIServices.mm; configured in AIServicesSettingsSheet.swift | Registered and configurable (host/port/https/model rows render via the property list). Practical value on iPad is low (requires a reachable LAN Ollama host) but it is fully wired, not stubbed. |
| Generic OpenAI-compatible client provider | Implemented | P3 | S | shared src-core/ai/GenericClient.cpp; surfaced via XLAIServices.mm | Registered with all four capabilities (Prompt/ColorPalette/Images/Speech2Text). Config rows render in AIServicesSettingsSheet. Images route through XLAIImageSession, lyrics through generateLyricTrack. |
| Apple Intelligence (on-device) provider | Implemented | P1 | S | shared src-core/ai/AppleIntelligence.cpp + macOS/src-apple-core/ai/AppleIntelligenceBridge.* / AppleSpeechRecognizer.swift, linked into iPad via libxLights-Apple-core.a | Comment in XLAIServices.mm:241-244 confirms ServiceManager registers AppleIntelligence on Apple Silicon for iPad too; capabilities self-gate by OS via __builtin_available. This is what powers on-device AI lyric transcription on iPad. Color palette (FoundationModels) and ImagePlayground image gen are available where OS supports them. |
| AI plugin DLL loading | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLAIServices.mm:240-245 (pluginDir passed as empty string) | OUT-OF-SCOPE: iOS App Store policy forbids loading executable code (dylib/DLL) from outside the signed app bundle; dynamic third-party provider plugins cannot ship on iPad. Documented in the bridge header. — Intentionally disabled: ServiceManager is constructed with an empty plugin directory so loadPlugins() finds nothing. |
| Services preferences panel (config + enable per capability) | Implemented | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/AIServicesSettingsSheet.swift (renders each service's GetProperties() as SwiftUI rows: Toggle/SecureField/TextField/Picker/IntField); reached from XLightsCommands.swift:269 Tools -> AI Services... | Full parity with the desktop ServicesPanel. Per-property change persists immediately via setBool/String/IntProperty -> SaveSettings, mirroring 'apply changes immediately'. Per-capability enable toggles render as Bool rows; category rows become Section headers. |
| Test service button | Implemented | P2 | S | src-iPad/App/AIServicesSettingsSheet.swift testSection + runTest(); bridge XLAIServices.mm testServiceAsync -> aiBase::TestLLM() | Dropdown of available services + Test button, runs TestLLM on a background queue, shows OK/Error. Matches desktop SetupTests/OnButtonTestClick. |
| Secret storage for API keys | Implemented | P2 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLiPadServiceSettingsStore (IServiceSettingsStore impl: plain settings -> NSUserDefaults, secrets -> iOS Keychain kSecAttrAccessibleAfterFirstUnlock); Secret-kind rows render as SecureField in AIServicesSettingsSheet.swift | Equivalent to desktop's wxSecretStore-backed WxServiceSettingsStore; Keychain replaces the macOS keychain on the desktop side. |
| AI Color Palette generation dialog | Partial | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/AIPaletteGenerationSheet.swift; bridge XLAIServices.mm generateColorPalette | Song/FreeForm modes, service picker, generate/regenerate, and a per-color swatch+name+description preview are all present and call core GenerateColorPalette. MISSING vs desktop: (1) the generator's GetProperties() options are NOT rendered, so the style picker is absent (see style-preset gap); (2) no crop, resize, or reset post-generation editing. These need a SwiftUI ParametersSizer-equivalent and an image-edit surface. |
| Image generator style presets | Missing | P2 | M | Style logic exists in shared core (src-core/ai/gemini.cpp:157-211, AppleIntelligence.cpp:162-201) but is not surfaced by src-iPad/App/AIImageGenerationSheet.swift | AIImageGenerationSheet calls XLAIImageSession.generate(prompt) directly and never reads the generator's GetProperties()/SetProperty, so the Gemini (cartoon/sticker/outline/neon) and Apple Intelligence (animation/illustration/sketch/emoji) style choices can't be chosen on iPad. Standalone save itself is lower priority than the flood-fill, which should ideally run even in embedded mode. |

Effort L mostly due to the MappingModelInfo extraction and validation, not the LLM call. |

Lower priority than structured mapping because the structured path (above) already covers Claude, the recommended mapping service; this fallback only matters for non-structured services. If structured mapping ships, this can stay desktop-only or be deferred. |

## 22. Automation, Scripting & REST API

_Parity summary._ iPad parity in this area is essentially zero today: there is no HTTP/REST server, no JSON command dispatcher, no Lua or Python engine, no Run Scripts UI, and no xlDo/CLI equivalent anywhere in src-iPad/ (verified by grep — zero matches for wxHTTPServer, sol::/lua_State, pybind11, xlDoAutomation, ProcessxlDoAutomation, or any network listener). The desktop automation stack lives entirely in src-ui-wx/automation/ (wx-dependent and bound to xLightsFrame), so none of it ports for free. The crucial mitigating fact is that the *underlying operations* behind nearly every automation command (openSequence, renderAll, addEffect, get/setEffectSettings, uploadController, runSequenceCheck, batch render, FSEQ export, etc.) already exist as wired XLSequenceDocument bridge methods — the missing piece is a dispatch/scripting layer on top of them, not the operations. liblua.a and libcurl.a are already shipped in the iOS deps, making an embedded Lua scripting engine genuinely feasible; a REST/HTTP server is technically possible on iOS but of low value, and the natural iOS automation idioms (App Intents / Shortcuts / URL schemes) are entirely unexplored.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| HTTP/REST automation server (A/B port) | Missing | P3 | L | — | No embedded HTTP server on iPad (grep for wxHTTPServer/StartAutomationListener/49913/NWListener/socket = zero hits). Could be built with Apple Network.framework instead of wxHTTPServer, but on a sandboxed single-window touch app the value of a localhost REST port is marginal — external tools rarely target an iPad, and an iPad in the foreground is what's being driven. The natural iOS replacement is App Intents/Shortcuts/URL schemes (also entirely absent). Mark low priority rather than out-of-scope: iOS does allow listening sockets, so it is technically possible if a use case (e.g. desktop xLights driving an iPad, or xSchedule-on-Mac talking to iPad) emerges. |
| Automation port preference (Disabled / Port A / Port B) | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: This preference only exists to configure the A/B HTTP listener and -a/-b launch flags. iPad has no command-line argv (verified: no cmdLine/argc/argv in src-iPad) and no listener; the dual A/B port scheme exists so two desktop instances + xFade/xSchedule can coexist on one machine, which is not an iPad scenario. — Only becomes relevant if/when the REST server feature is built; otherwise nothing to configure. |
| xlDoAutomation JSON command dispatch (ProcessxlDoAutomation) | Missing | P2 | L | — | This is the keystone gap. Desktop's xLightsFrame::ProcessxlDoAutomation (xLightsAutomations.cpp:1298) is the central JSON cmd dispatcher that both the REST server AND the Lua RunCommand host function call into. It is wx-bound and tied to xLightsFrame, so it does not exist on iPad. The win: the ~40 commands it dispatches are mostly thin wrappers over operations that ALREADY exist as XLSequenceDocument bridge methods (openSequence, renderAll, saveSequence, addEffectToRow, effectSettingsForRow/setEffectSettingValue, uploadOutputForController, runSequenceCheck, writeFseq, loadShowFolder, etc., all confirmed present). Building a wx-free JSON dispatcher in the bridge that maps cmd+params onto these existing methods is the single highest-leverage item and unlocks Lua scripting. Effort is L mostly because of the surface area (mapping each command + JSON in/out marshalling), not new core work. |
| Command: getVersion | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (appVersion / currentAppVersion) | The underlying value exists (XLSequenceDocument exposes appVersion/currentAppVersion), but there is no command-dispatch surface to invoke it as a 'getVersion' automation command. Trivial to expose once the dispatcher (ProcessxlDoAutomation equivalent) exists. |

FindSequence-style search is implicit in the show-folder scan already used by SequencePickerView. Needs the dispatcher layer. |
| Command: closeSequence | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (closeSequence, isSequenceDirty) | closeSequence + isSequenceDirty exist; the force/quiet flag handling and 504-on-unsaved semantics would be implemented in the dispatcher wrapper. |
| Command: newSequence | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (newSequenceAtPath:type:mediaPath:durationMS:frameMS:) | Core operation fully wired (used by NewSequenceWizardView). The 'refuse if open unless force' guard and optional view selection are dispatcher-level. Needs command wrapper only. |
| Command: saveSequence | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (saveSequence, saveSequenceAs:) | saveSequence and saveSequenceAs both exist. Save-vs-SaveAs branching on a 'seq' param is dispatcher logic. Needs command wrapper only. |
| Command: saveLayout | Partial | P3 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (saveLayoutChanges) | saveLayoutChanges persists model/effects xml; the networks/controller file save also happens through the layout editor save path. Combined single-call command wrapper missing. Low priority as an automation command. |
| Command: renderAll | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (renderAll, isRenderDone, renderProgressFraction, abortRenderAndWait:) | renderAll + progress + blocking wait all exist and are exercised by the live UI. The highdef=true flag would be partial: iPadRenderContext hard-codes IsLowDefinitionRender()==true (deliberate perf choice), so the temporary high-def override would need plumbing/eval before honoring highdef. Command wrapper missing. |
| Command: batchRender | Partial | P2 | M | src-iPad/App/BatchRenderRunner.swift, BatchRenderSheet.swift; XLSequenceDocument open/renderAll/saveSequence | Interactive batch render is fully WIRED on iPad (BatchRenderRunner does open->render->save sequentially with progress). The hard part (the batch open/render/save loop) already exists; only the command-dispatch entry point is needed. |
| Command: checkSequence | Partial | P3 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (runSequenceCheckWithProgress:); src-iPad/App/CheckSequenceSheet.swift | Check Sequence runs on iPad via src-core/diagnostics/SequenceChecker (covers desktop minus wx-only network/OS sections) and returns structured issues. The automation command returns a generated report FILE path; iPad returns issues in-memory, so a wrapper would need to serialize issues to a report file. Command wrapper + report writer missing. |

Only command wrappers + key-name normalization needed. |
| Command: deleteAllAliases | Partial | P3 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (setModelAliases: per model) | Aliases are settable per model (setModelAliases:); a delete-all-across-every-model command would iterate allModelNamesInShow clearing each. The bulk command wrapper + affected-model list return are missing. Marginal. |
| Command: getViews / makeMaster | Partial | P3 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (availableViews); src-iPad/App/DisplayElementsSheet.swift | View listing exists (availableViews) and the full views editor (DisplayElementsSheet) is wired. 'Make Master' (DoMakeMaster on a named view) does not appear as a discrete bridge op — would need a small bridge addition plus the command wrapper. Low value. |
| Command: addEffect | Partial | P1 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (addEffectToRow:name:startMS:endMS: and addEffectToRow:name:settings:palette:startMS:endMS:) | Fully wired core op including the settings+palette paste variant and undo registration; layer auto-creation handled by the layer-CRUD bridge methods. Only the JSON command wrapper (resolving a target element/layer descriptor to a row index) is missing. Higher priority because effect authoring is the heart of scripted sequence generation. |
| Command: getEffectIDs | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (effectCountForRow:, effectCountOnRow:, per-layer enumeration) | Per-layer effect enumeration exists; effects carry stable IDs in core. A bridge getter returning the nested per-layer ID array plus the command wrapper are the only missing pieces. |
| Command: getEffectSettings / setEffectSettings | Partial | P1 | M | src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (effectSettingsForRow:atIndex:, effectPaletteForRow:atIndex:, replaceEffectSettings:palette:inRow:atIndex:, moveEffectInRow:..., effect name/start/end getters) | All constituent reads (name/settings/palette/start/end/selected) and mutations (rename, re-time via moveEffect, replace settings/palette via replaceEffectSettings) exist as bridge methods. The desktop command keys by model+layer+effectID; the iPad bridge keys by row+index, so the wrapper needs an ID->index resolver. High value for scripted effect editing. |
| Command: cloneModelEffects | Missing | P2 | S | — | No CloneXLightsEffects (copy all effects model->model, optional erase) bridge method found. The core CloneXLightsEffects logic is reusable; needs a thin wx-free bridge wrapper + command wrapper. Medium value for layout-change workflows. |
| Command: importXLightsSequence (.xmap mapping import) | Partial | P2 | M | src-iPad/Bridge/XLImportSession (loadSourceSequenceAtPath:, setMappingForRow:, runAutoMap, applyImportWithEraseExisting:lock:); src-iPad/App/ImportEffectsView.swift | Real xLights sequence effect import (interactive mapping, auto-map, .xmaphint) is fully WIRED via XLImportSession running the real EffectMapper. The automation command takes a pre-supplied .xmap mapping file and applies headlessly; the iPad session builds mappings interactively/auto rather than loading an .xmap. Headless .xmap-file path + command wrapper are missing; underlying import engine present. |
| Command: runScript | Missing | P2 | M | — | Depends on a Lua engine, which does not exist on iPad yet. Once a wx-free LuaRunner is built (liblua.a is shipped for iOS), running a .lua file by path is straightforward. Blocked by the Lua scripting engine item. |
| Command: closexLights | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: iOS apps cannot programmatically terminate themselves (Apple HIG/App Store: calling exit() is rejected; the OS owns app lifecycle). There is no equivalent of posting wxID_EXIT. — The unsaved-changes guard semantics map to the existing close/dirty prompt, but the actual quit cannot be honored on iOS. |
| Internal automation request helper (xLightsRequest) | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: A wx helper (wxUtilities.cpp) that builds a URL to the local automation port and issues a request, used so xLights' own components/companion apps can drive automation over HTTP. iPad has no automation port and drives the core directly via the in-process XLSequenceDocument bridge, making an HTTP self-call pointless. — The iPad equivalent of 'drive automation locally' is simply calling the bridge method directly — no HTTP round-trip needed, so this helper has no place on iPad. |
| Lua scripting engine (RunScript / sol2 interpreter) | Missing | P2 | L | — | No Lua anywhere in src-iPad (zero sol::/lua_State hits). FEASIBLE: liblua.a is already present in /opt/xLights-macOS-dependencies/lib-ios/, so the interpreter can be embedded. The desktop LuaRunner is wx-coupled (#include xLightsMain.h, wx/stdpaths.h) and tied to xLightsFrame, so it needs a wx-free reimplementation built on XLSequenceDocument. The big dependency is the JSON command dispatcher (see ProcessxlDoAutomation gap) since Lua's RunCommand just forwards to it. package.path would point at a sandbox scripts folder. App Store-safe (Lua bytecode is interpreted data, not downloaded native code, mirroring how it's already used for effect/show logic). |
| Lua host function: RunCommand | Missing | P2 | M | — | RunCommand bridges Lua to ProcessxlDoAutomation and returns the JSON response as a Lua table. Blocked by both the Lua engine and the JSON command dispatcher gaps. Trivial once those exist; it's the glue line LuaRunner.cpp:218-221. |
| Lua host functions: user prompts (ShowMessage/PromptOption/PromptString/PromptSelection/PromptSequences) | Missing | P3 | M | — | Desktop uses wxMessageBox/wxTextEntryDialog/BatchRenderDialog. On iPad these would be SwiftUI alerts/sheets driven from the script runner; the underlying pickers (e.g. BatchRenderSheet) exist. Requires a synchronous-prompt-from-background-script bridging pattern (script thread <-> main-actor SwiftUI), which is the fiddly part. Blocked by the Lua engine. |
| Lua host functions: data/string helpers + Log (SplitString/JoinString/JSONToTable/TableToJSON/Log) | Missing | P3 | S | — | Pure data helpers with no UI dependency; would be reimplemented inside a wx-free LuaRunner (JSONToTable/TableToJSON over nlohmann/json which is already a core dep). Blocked only by the Lua engine existing. Small once it does. |
| Python scripting engine (pybind11 / embedded CPython) | Out-of-scope | P3 | XL | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: Embedding CPython on iOS is barred in practice: App Store guideline 2.5.2 forbids downloading/executing code that changes app behavior, and a general-purpose Python interpreter that runs arbitrary user .py files runs afoul of that; CPython/pybind11 are also not provided in the iOS deps (confirmed: no python lib in lib-ios). Desktop already compiles it only when Python.h is present. — Lua is the App-Store-acceptable scripting path; Python should stay desktop-only. |
| Run Scripts dialog (Tools > Run Scripts) | Missing | P3 | M | — | No Run Scripts UI on iPad (ScriptsDialog is wx; Tools menu in XLightsCommands.swift is an explicit placeholder lacking this entry). Would be a SwiftUI sheet listing .lua scripts from the sandbox scripts folder with a live log pane. Blocked by the Lua engine. The log pane pattern already exists (LogViewerSheet). |
| Run Scripts: script header/about parsing | Missing | P3 | S | — | Reads the leading Lua comment block for an About blurb. Pure text parsing, trivial to port, but only meaningful inside a Run Scripts UI. Blocked by that dialog. |
| Run Scripts: Download scripts from GitHub | Missing | P3 | M | — | Desktop fetches community scripts via GitHub API + CurlManager and downloads into the user script folder. iPad has HTTPS download patterns already (vendor catalog, stem model, LRCLIB) so the fetch/multi-select/download flow is reproducible, but it's only useful once Run Scripts exists. Blocked by the Lua engine + dialog. |
| Run Scripts: View Script / Open Folder context menu | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: Desktop opens the script in the system editor and reveals the containing folder in Finder. iOS has no concept of 'reveal in Finder' or a registered external text editor for an arbitrary file; the Files app share/quick-look is the closest idiom. — Could surface a read-only QuickLook/share instead, but the literal 'open in editor / reveal folder' actions don't exist on iOS. |
| Run Scripts: Refresh / Clear log | Missing | P3 | S | — | Trivial UI affordances (rescan scripts folder; clear log pane) inside the Run Scripts dialog. Blocked by that dialog existing. |
| xlDo command-line tool | Out-of-scope | P3 | L | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: xlDo is a standalone CLI binary (separate target, not built for iOS) that talks to a running xLights over its localhost automation port. iOS has no shell/CLI for users to invoke a binary, no general process spawning, and no automation port on iPad. The whole tool presupposes a desktop/server environment. — The iOS-native analog would be App Intents / Shortcuts actions, which is a different (unbuilt) feature, not a port of xlDo. |
| xlDo: template files with %P1..%P9 parameter substitution | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: A feature of the xlDo CLI (parameter substitution into a JSON template before sending over the automation port). No CLI, no template-invocation surface, and no automation port on iPad. — Tied to the out-of-scope xlDo tool. |
| xlDo: -s output script generation (set/EXPORT vars) | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: Writes returned JSON values into a shell/batch script (set/EXPORT) for a calling shell to consume. There is no shell environment on iOS to consume such output. — Tied to the out-of-scope xlDo tool. |
| xlDo: startxLights launcher command | Out-of-scope | P3 | M | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: Launches the xLights executable on a chosen port (platform-specific exec) and polls until it responds. iOS does not allow one app to exec/launch another app's binary or pass launch flags; app launching goes through the OS, and there are no automation ports. — Tied to the out-of-scope xlDo tool and the desktop launch-flag model. |
| App launch: headless render (-r) and check-sequence (-cs) | Out-of-scope | P3 | L | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: iOS apps have no command-line argv and cannot run headless/exit-on-completion (no UI session = no app on iOS; the OS terminates background-only foreground apps, and self-exit is forbidden). Verified: no cmdLine/argc/argv handling in src-iPad. — The underlying render and check operations exist (renderAll, runSequenceCheckWithProgress:); only the headless-from-CLI invocation model is impossible. The interactive equivalents (Batch Render, Check Sequence) already exist on iPad. |
| App launch: -a/-b port, -o output-on, -s/-m dirs, -w wipe | Out-of-scope | P3 | M | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: All are command-line switches; iOS provides no argv to the app. Show/media dirs, output-on, and settings reset are all reachable through the iPad UI (FolderConfigView, output toggle), just not via launch flags. — The capabilities (set show/media folder, output on, etc.) exist in-app; only the launch-flag delivery mechanism is unavailable. |
| App launch: read-only packaged sequence (.zip/.xsqz) | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/App/XLightsApp.swift (.onOpenURL for .xsqz/.zip/.piz -> openPackagedSequence); src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.h (openPackagedSequence:, isPackagedSequence) | iPad DOES open packaged sequences (.xsqz/.zip/.piz) via .onOpenURL -> copy-to-sandbox -> openPackagedSequence, extracting to a temp show folder. The difference vs desktop: iPad re-packs on save (copySandboxBackToOriginal) rather than forcing strict read-only/saving-disabled mode. Effectively present; the explicit read-only-lock semantic is the only nuance, hence partial rather than implemented. |
| Internal automation request helper (xLightsRequest) | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: A wx helper (wxUtilities.cpp) that builds a URL to the local automation port and issues a request, used so xLights' own components/companion apps can drive automation over HTTP. iPad has no automation port and drives the core directly via the in-process XLSequenceDocument bridge, making an HTTP self-call pointless. — DUPLICATE of the earlier xLightsRequest row in the source data; preserved verbatim. The iPad equivalent of 'drive automation locally' is simply calling the bridge method directly. |

## 23. Jukebox, Effect Presets & Effect Tree

_Parity summary._ Parity in this area is low. The Jukebox is entirely absent on iPad (no panel, no playback, no bridge wiring) even though the shared core JukeboxButtonData round-trips its data through the .xsq, so assignments persist but are invisible/unusable. Effect Presets exist only as a session-only, flat, single-effect store in SequencerViewModel (save/apply/delete via the grid long-press menu) — there is no on-disk persistence, no group/tree hierarchy, no GIF previews, no rename/reorder/import/export/update, and no apply-mode selection. The one genuinely solid piece is effect creation: EffectPaletteView (tap-to-arm + tap-to-place, plus a random dice button) is a working touch analog of the desktop Effect Dropper, achieving the same goal without drag-drop icons.

| Feature | Status | Priority | Effort | iPad Location | Notes/Reason |
|---------|--------|----------|--------|---------------|--------------|
| Effect Presets tree panel (browse hierarchy) | Missing | P1 | L | — | iPad has only a flat session-only list (SequencerViewModel.swift presets: [EffectPreset], struct l2988) surfaced as flat 'Apply Preset:' buttons in the grid long-press menu (SequencerGridV2View.swift l589, l674). No hierarchical tree, no group nesting, no layer-count/duration annotations. Needs a real presets browser sheet/panel plus a model layer. EffectTreeDialog/EffectPresetManager are wx-only (src-ui-wx/sequencer/EffectTreeDialog.cpp), so the data model + serialization either need porting to src-core/ or reimplementing in the bridge. The savedPalettes/savedValueCurves file-store pattern already on the bridge is a usable template. |
| Open/toggle Effect Presets panel (View menu + grid right-click) | Partial | P1 | S | src-iPad/App/SequencerGridV2View.swift (l589, l674); src-iPad/App/XLightsCommands.swift | Presets are reachable only via 'Apply Preset:' entries inside the effect long-press menu. There is no View-menu entry to open a dedicated presets panel/sheet (XLightsCommands.swift View menu has no preset item). Once a presets browser exists, add a menu/toolbar entry to open it. |
| New Preset from current/selected effects | Partial | P1 | M | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift saveSelectedEffectAsPreset (l3004); SequencerGridV2View.swift 'Save as Preset…' alert (l1087) | Captures only ONE selected effect's settings+palette (uses selectedEffect, not a multi-effect selection), so it cannot save multi-effect/multi-layer presets the way desktop's GetPresetData does (which serializes the whole selection with LAYER markers). No group-target selection, no save to disk. Needs multi-effect capture + persistence. Desktop GetPresetData/GetSelectedEffectsData live in src-ui-wx/sequencer/MainSequencer.cpp (wx layer) so the serialization needs a core/bridge equivalent. |
| Apply preset to grid (button + double-click + grid menu) | Partial | P1 | M | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift applyPreset (l3032); SequencerGridV2View.swift l589/l674 | Apply works for single-effect presets onto the current effect selection (matching type -> replace settings/palette via replaceEffectSettings; differing type -> delete + re-add). But it applies to the SELECTED effect(s), not a drop location, and cannot apply multi-layer presets (no LAYER-marker paste path). Desktop's ApplyEffectsPreset -> EffectsGrid::Paste with layer structure is not wired. Needs multi-layer apply + apply-at-drop-location support. |

| Update Preset from current selection | Missing | P2 | S | — | deletePreset exists (SequencerViewModel.swift l3079) and saveSelectedEffectAsPreset overwrites a same-named preset (l3018), which is a partial substitute, but there is no explicit 'Update Preset' op against a selected preset leaf. Cheap to add once a preset browser exposes selection. |
| Rename preset or group | Missing | P2 | S | — | No rename UI/op. EffectPreset.name is settable but no rename flow exists. Trivial to add alongside a presets browser; validation (forbidden FS chars, uniqueness) should be ported from EffectPresetManager/PromptForName once presets persist to disk. |
| Delete preset or group (button + Delete key) | Partial | P2 | S | src-iPad/App/SequencerViewModel.swift deletePreset (l3079) | deletePreset removes from the in-memory store, but it is not surfaced in any UI today (no delete button/swipe), there are no groups to delete recursively, and no GIF cleanup. Needs UI surface + persistence-aware delete once presets are on disk. |
| Add preset group | Missing | P2 | M | — | iPad presets are a flat list with no grouping concept. Requires introducing a group/tree data model (port of EffectPresetManager hierarchy) plus UI. Bundled with the tree-panel work. |
| Drag-and-drop reorganize presets/groups in tree | Missing | P3 | L | — | No tree, so no drag-to-reorganize. Depends on the tree model + group support landing first; SwiftUI drag-drop reorder is feasible but is downstream of the core data model. Auto-expand-on-hover and GIF rename are extra polish. |
| Reorder presets/groups via Top/Up/Down/Bottom buttons | Missing | P3 | S | — | No ordering UI. Once a persisted ordered model exists, move-up/down/top/bottom (or SwiftUI .onMove) is straightforward (mirrors EffectTreeDialog MoveNode). |
| Sort presets (Sort Group / Sort All) | Missing | P3 | S | — | No sort op; depends on tree/group model. Low value; alphabetical sort is trivial once the hierarchy exists. |
| Search presets by name | Missing | P3 | S | — | No search field. With a real preset list a SwiftUI .searchable filter is trivial; case-insensitive name match mirrors EffectTreeDialog SearchForText. |
| Animated GIF preview of preset | Missing | P2 | L | — | No preset previews at all. iPad already has the full RenderEngine via iPadRenderContext (could render a preset onto a hidden 64x64 matrix like desktop's EnsurePresetModel/LoadPresetEffects), but WriteGIFForPreset is in wx TabConvert.cpp. iPad has no GIF encoder wired; would render frames + encode (e.g. via ImageIO/CGImageDestination GIF) and display. Meaningful effort; consider an animated thumbnail rather than literal GIF on disk. |
| Hide preset preview setting | Missing | P3 | S | — | No preview at all yet, so no toggle. Add an @AppStorage flag if/when GIF previews land. |
