| Import presets from .xpreset or rgbeffects file | Missing | P2 | M | — | No preset import. iPad already has robust file-picker + import patterns (ImportEffectsView, .xtiming import, palette/.xvc import via savedPalettes). The .xpreset/rgbeffects parse logic is in EffectPresetManager (wx-ish) and needs core/bridge exposure. Depends on a persisted preset model existing. |
| Export presets/group to .xpreset | Missing | P2 | M | — | No export. Needs the persisted preset model + serialization (FileSerializingVisitor / EffectPresetItem::Save are in src-ui-wx). iPad fileExporter/share-sheet plumbing already exists (PackageSequence, exportTimingTrack) to handle the file output side. |
| Preset name validation & auto-fix on load | Missing | P2 | S | — | saveSelectedEffectAsPreset only trims whitespace and overwrites same-named entries (SequencerViewModel.swift l3005-3022); no forbidden-FS-char stripping, no on-load auto-fix, no uniqueness-within-group check. Relevant once presets persist to disk; port FixName/NameCollissionInGroup logic. |
| Button enable/disable state logic (ValidateWindow) | Missing | P3 | S | — | No panel with the apply/update/delete/export buttons whose enablement this governs. Becomes a natural part of building the preset browser (disable group-only ops, etc.). |
| Jukebox panel (50 numbered playback buttons) | Missing | P2 | L | — | No jukebox UI anywhere in src-iPad/ (confirmed via grep — zero references). The shared core src-core/render/JukeboxButtonData.h (LoadJukeboxButtons/SaveJukeboxButtons) round-trips the <Jukebox> node through SequenceFile, so assignments persist in the .xsq but are invisible/unusable on iPad. Building the panel needs: bridge methods to read/write the JukeboxButtonMap, a SwiftUI reflowing button grid, and looped playback wiring (iPad already has looped playback infra: loop-region play, audioPlaySegment, output). JukeboxPanel.cpp is wx-only. |
| Link Jukebox button to an effect (by Model/Layer/Time or Description) | Missing | P2 | M | — | No link dialog. The cascading Model/Layer/Time lookups need new bridge methods analogous to desktop's GetAllElementNamesWithEffects/GetElementLayerCount/GetElementLayerEffects (the underlying SequenceElements data is already in iPadRenderContext). LinkJukeboxButtonDialog.cpp is wx-only. Depends on the jukebox panel existing. |
| Jukebox effect playback (looped) with two lookup strategies | Missing | P2 | M | — | No playback. iPad has looped playback + output infra (toggleOutput/sendOutputFrame, loop-region play in SequencerViewModel/transport), so wiring 'select matching effect by description or M/L/T then play looped, AllOff on miss' is feasible once the panel + link data exist. EffectsGrid::PlayLoopedEffect is wx; iPad would replicate via its own transport. |
| Jukebox keyboard shortcuts (buttons 1-5) | Missing | P3 | S | — | No jukebox, so no shortcuts. iPad supports hardware-keyboard commands (XLightsCommands.swift) so adding JUKEBOX_BTN_1..5 equivalents is trivial once playback exists. Marginal value on a touch device. |
| Jukebox persistence in sequence file | Implemented | P3 | S | src-core/render/JukeboxButtonData.h (shared core, linked by iPad) | The <Jukebox> XML node load/save is in shared src-core via SequenceFile, so jukebox assignments round-trip through the iPad's open/save unchanged even today — data is preserved. However iPad has no UI/bridge to view or sync to/from this map (JukeboxPanel SyncFromData/SyncToData are wx), so the data is inert until a panel is built. Marking implemented for the persistence layer specifically; the UI sync is covered by the panel gap above. |
| Jukebox tooltip/state export for xSchedule | Out-of-scope | P3 | S | — | OUT-OF-SCOPE: This surface (SetLabel('XLIGHTS_JUKEBOX'), pipe/JSON tooltip+state strings, EVT_PLAYJUKEBOXITEM) exists solely so the desktop xSchedule companion app can read the panel via wx label introspection. xSchedule has moved to its own repo and there is no xSchedule on iPad, so this inter-app IPC contract has no consumer on iOS. — Out of scope: this is a wx-label IPC contract for the (desktop-only, separate-repo) xSchedule app; no consumer exists on iPad. Nothing to port. |
| Effect Dropper panel (drag effect icons onto grid) | Implemented | P0 | S | src-iPad/App/EffectPaletteView.swift; SequencerViewModel.swift addEffectFromPaletteTap (l4936), selectPaletteEffect (l5663), availableEffects (l318) | iPad uses a touch idiom instead of drag-drop: a horizontal palette of effect-name buttons (from document.availableEffectNames) that you tap to arm, then tap on the grid to place (snaps to active timing cell / neighbors). Plus a random 'dice' button. Functionally equivalent to the desktop dropper for the core goal (create any effect at a location). It shows text names rather than effect icons (icon bitmaps are available via iconBGRAForEffectNamed on the bridge if a visual upgrade is wanted). Also double-tap-to-create on the grid exists. Considered implemented for parity of purpose; the icon-button visual is the only minor gap. |
| Effect icon caching / tooltip per effect | Partial | P3 | M | src-iPad/App/EffectPaletteView.swift (text labels); src-iPad/Bridge/XLSequenceDocument.mm iconBGRAForEffectNamed:desiredSize:outputSize: | The effect-creation palette shows text names, not the cached effect icons; icons ARE rendered in the timeline grid (EffectsMetalGridView via iconBGRAForEffectNamed) and the bridge can supply per-effect BGRA icons, so upgrading EffectPaletteView to icon buttons is straightforward. No per-button tooltip (touch idiom; long-press could surface the effect name/description). The drag-cursor-is-the-icon behavior is a desktop drag-drop concept with no touch analog. |

## Rollup A — P0 Missing / Partial Features

- **Edit Operations** — Undo (_Partial_)
- **Edit Operations** — Redo (_Partial_)
- **Sequencer: Timing Tracks & Waveform** — Add Timing Track dialog (fixed-interval + special types) (_Partial_)

## Rollup B — Out-of-Scope Features and Reasons

- **File & Sequence Lifecycle** — Revert To... versioned backups (macOS): macOS-only NSDocument/NSFileVersion revision API; iOS has no equivalent automatic file-version history for app-managed files outside iCloud's own version store, which isn't exposed the same way.
- **File & Sequence Lifecycle** — Export House Preview Video: Desktop encoder lives in wx-only src-ui-wx and relies on FFmpeg encode (not in src-core). iPad could in principle build an AVAssetWriter exporter from the Metal house preview, but that is net-new XL work with no shared-core reuse, so it's effectively out-of-scope for parity rather than a simple wiring task.
- **File & Sequence Lifecycle** — Open New xLights Instance: iOS apps are single-process; you cannot spawn a second independent application instance. Multi-scene windows exist but share one process/app state, so a truly separate second instance isn't possible on iPad.
- **Tools Menu** — HinksPix Export: HinksPix export's primary output is writing HSEQ/playlists/schedule to a removable SD/USB card (with a Refresh USB Drives picker). iOS provides no API to enumerate/write raw removable drives, and HinksPix uses proprietary (non-open) controller firmware/protocol, which is outside the FPP/ESPixelStick open-firmware scope the iPad bridge deliberately limits itself to. Combined with the foreign-controller daughter-board targeting, this is a desktop-only workflow.
- **Tools Menu** — HinksPix Controllers tab + multi-controller targeting: Foreign1/Foreign2 daughter-controller assignment and target-drive selection are intrinsic to the HinksPix proprietary-controller + removable-media workflow that iOS cannot serve (no raw drive enumeration; proprietary firmware out of scope).
- **Tools Menu** — HinksPix Playlists tab (build/order/save playlists): Only meaningful as input to the HinksPix .ply card/controller output, which is desktop-only (removable-media + proprietary firmware). No standalone value on iPad.
- **Tools Menu** — HinksPix Schedule tab: The day/time schedule grid is written to the HinksPix controller/card schedule, which depends on the desktop-only proprietary-controller + removable-media output path.
- **Tools Menu** — HinksPix Export to SD Card vs Upload to controller (Refresh USB Drives): iOS exposes no API to enumerate or write to raw removable SD/USB drives (the 'Refresh USB Drives'/'Export to SD Card' path), so the primary HinksPix output channel cannot be implemented on iPad.
- **Tools Menu** — Run Scripts (Lua / Python automation): Running user-supplied/downloaded interpreted scripts (Lua VM, Python) that drive the app conflicts with App Store Review guideline 2.5.2 (apps may not download or execute code that changes app behavior). The whole point of the feature is executing arbitrary downloaded community scripts, which is exactly what's prohibited. Embedding a sandboxed Lua engine for built-in-only scripts could be argued, but the user-download library management makes the feature as designed out of scope.
- **Tools Menu** — Run Scripts library management (refresh / view / download): Downloading additional community automation scripts to execute is the App-Store-prohibited behavior (2.5.2); the library management exists only to feed the script runner that can't ship.
- **View / Windows / Perspectives** — Reset Toolbars: iPad has no wxAUI toolbars to reset. The toolbar set is a fixed SwiftUI layout and a menu bar; there is no draggable/dockable AUI toolbar state to persist or restore, so the command has nothing to act on.
- **View / Windows / Perspectives** — Perspectives: Save Current: A perspective is a wxAUI SavePerspective() geometry string describing dock/float/tab/size of ~17 panes. iPad has no AUI manager and a fixed split-pane layout (only Preview/Inspector toggles + detach-to-scene), so there is no arbitrary pane geometry to capture. The iPad equivalents (pane widths/heights, detached-scene state) are already persisted via @AppStorage automatically.
- **View / Windows / Perspectives** — Perspectives: Save As New: Same root cause as Save Current: there is no wxAUI layout to snapshot under a name. Named layout presets would require building an entirely new iPad-side layout-state model (which panes detached, sidebar widths) and a persistence/switch UI — not a port of any shared core, and of low value given the constrained iPad layout.
- **View / Windows / Perspectives** — Perspectives: Edit/Load (Perspectives manager panel): The Perspectives manager add/delete/rename/save/load list operates on wxAUI perspective strings stored in rgbeffects. With no AUI docking on iPad there is nothing for it to manage. Could be re-conceived as named iPad-layout presets but that is net-new design, not a parity port.
- **View / Windows / Perspectives** — Perspectives: Auto Save (per-machine): The desktop feature auto-saves a wxAUI perspective string per machine. iPad has no AUI string; its analogous live-layout persistence (pane sizes, which scenes are detached) is already always-on and handled natively, so a toggle for it is both unnecessary and inapplicable.
- **View / Windows / Perspectives** — Perspectives: dynamic per-perspective menu list / quick switch: Depends entirely on the saved-perspectives list, which does not exist on iPad (no AUI). Nothing to populate the radio-item submenu from.
- **View / Windows / Perspectives** — Suppress Dock: House Preview: This forces a wxAUI pane to stay floating instead of docking. iPad has no AUI docking; previews are either embedded in the fixed layout or detached into a separate iPadOS WindowGroup scene. There is no dock-vs-float-vs-suppress state machine for the user to constrain.
- **View / Windows / Perspectives** — Suppress Dock: Model Preview: Same as House Preview suppress-dock: no wxAUI docking model on iPad, so there is no floating-only state to enforce. Detach-to-scene is the iPad equivalent and is user-controlled per-instance.
- **View / Windows / Perspectives** — Windows: Perspectives shortcut item: Duplicate entry point to the Perspectives manager, which itself is out-of-scope (no wxAUI layout to manage).
- **View / Windows / Perspectives** — Perspective layout engine (wxAUI dock/float/persist): wxAUI arbitrary docking/floating/tabbing with serialized perspective strings (and the macOS gray-Metal re-dock workaround) is a wxWidgets-desktop construct with no iPadOS equivalent — iPadOS windowing is scene-based (Stage Manager / Split View), not free-form docking. The capability is intentionally re-implemented with platform-native idioms rather than ported; building a true AUI-style dock manager in SwiftUI would be an enormous effort against the grain of the platform.
- **Layout: Model Types & Properties** — Custom Model Method Picker (macOS): This is a macOS-AppKit-specific helper dialog (src-ui-wx/mac/CustomModelMethodPickerDialog.cpp) for choosing the custom-model creation method on the desktop Mac build. iPad's Add-Model flow (AddModelSheet + Map-from-Lights) is its own native entry point, so there is nothing to port — the picker is a desktop UI affordance, not a feature.
- **Layout: Preview, Background & View Objects** — SpaceMouse / 3Dconnexion 6-DOF navigation: iPadOS has no 3Dconnexion HID driver or public 6-DOF input API; the SpaceMouse SDK is desktop-only (Windows/macOS). Multi-touch + Pencil gestures are the native iPad equivalent.
- **Layout: Preview, Background & View Objects** — Double-click to maximize preview pane: iPadOS has no resizable in-window AUI pane to maximize/restore; windowing is OS-managed (Stage Manager / full-screen scenes), so a maximize-on-double-tap idiom doesn't apply. Double-tap is repurposed for camera reset.
- **Sequencer: Grid & Effect Editing** — Effect status / hover tooltip: Touch UI has no hover/cursor state or status bar; desktop hover tooltips and cursor-zone feedback don't translate to a finger-driven grid.
- **Sequencer: Timing Tracks & Waveform** — Download VAMP plugins prompt: VAMP plugins are downloadable external dynamic libraries; loading third-party native code at runtime is prohibited by iOS App Store policy (same reason AI plugin dylib loading is disabled on iOS). The download prompt has no purpose without a loadable-plugin host.
- **Sequencer: Rows / Display Elements / Views** — VAMP plugin timing tracks: VAMP analysis relies on loadable Queen Mary plugin dylibs; the App Store prohibits loading external code/plugins on iOS (same constraint that disables AI-plugin DLLs). iPad instead ships native on-device analyzers (onsets/tempo/chords/pitch/SNClassify) that cover the common use cases.
- **Color, Palettes & Value Curves** — Custom HSV/RGB color picker dialog: iOS provides a rich native color picker (UIColorPickerViewController via SwiftUI ColorPicker) that is the platform-standard idiom; building a custom HSV-disc dialog would fight the OS and add no user value.
- **Color, Palettes & Value Curves** — Reset panel when changing effects: This is a desktop wxConfig-backed UI preference for the persistent docked ColorPanel; the iPad inspector rebuilds per-selection and has no equivalent persistent panel/config to reset, so the behavior has no meaning on iPad.
- **Color, Palettes & Value Curves** — Palette display size preference (Normal/Large): This pref exists to manage limited horizontal space in the desktop's fixed-width docked ColorPanel; the iPad inspector lays palette rows full-width and touch-sized with dynamic type, so a manual size toggle has no purpose.
- **Import / Export (sequences & data)** — Convert log / status reporting: ConvertLogDialog is the status surface for the Convert dialog, which is itself deferred/missing on iPad. iPad already has a live spdlog View Log sheet (LogViewerSheet.swift) and import-error alerts, so a dedicated conversion-log dialog is only meaningful once/if the Convert dialog is ported. No standalone need.
- **Media & Audio** — Incompatible-video conversion on import: VideoTranscoder/MediaCompatibility transcode path is desktop-only; the bridge documents that iPad cannot convert incompatible video. No FFmpeg encode path is built into the iPad lib. iPad should warn-and-skip rather than transcode in place.
- **Media & Audio** — Audio output device selection: iOS does not expose per-app selectable audio output devices the way SDL/AVAudioEngine device enumeration does on desktop; routing is controlled by the OS (AVAudioSession / Control Center / AirPlay), not by the app. A device-picker UI would have nothing meaningful to enumerate.
- **Media & Audio** — VAMP plugin timing-track generation: xLightsVamp is explicitly desktop-only (src-core/media/xLightsVamp.h gated). VAMP loads external Queen Mary plugin .dylibs at runtime, which is not permitted under the iOS App Store sandbox (no loading of non-bundled dynamic libraries). The native detectors are the iOS replacement.
- **Media & Audio** — Export rendered sequence as video: GenericVideoExporter (src-ui-wx/media/VideoExporter) is a wx-UI desktop component and relies on the FFmpeg encode path that the iPad lib does not build (the bridge explicitly marks video transcode/encode desktop-only). Rendering+muxing video on-device would need an AVAssetWriter-based reimplementation; deferred and not a parity blocker for sequencing.
- **Controllers: Upload Protocols** — Bulk upload ESC cancel: No physical ESC key in the primary touch idiom; replace with an on-screen Cancel button when the bulk dialog is built, not a key handler.
- **Render Engine & FSEQ Export** — fseq_convert standalone tool: iOS has no user-facing command line / shell; a standalone CLI binary cannot be shipped or invoked in the App Store sandbox. The underlying FSEQFile conversion code is shared, so equivalent functionality could be offered as an in-app action if ever needed, but the CLI tool itself is not applicable to iPad.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Effect Assist Window mode: There is no Effect Assist panel on iPad. The desktop Effect Assist is a docked AUI pane (custom per-effect coordinate editors); iPad uses inline custom rows in the inspector (e.g. XYCenterPadView, MorphLineEditorRowView) instead of a separate assist window, so an Always-On/Off/Auto mode choice has nothing to govern.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Auto Show House Preview: iPad has no floating/auto-appearing House Preview window concept — the house preview is an embedded pane in SequencerView (or a detached scene the user explicitly opens). There is no auto-show-on-event behavior to toggle; window/scene management is governed by iPadOS scene lifecycle, not an app preference.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Disable key acceleration when held down: This governs keyboard key-repeat acceleration for navigation keys. iPad is touch-first; hardware-keyboard key-repeat behavior is managed by iPadOS and not something the app meaningfully tunes. Marginal even on desktop.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Zoom To Cursor: There is no mouse cursor on iPad; pinch-zoom always centers on the gesture centroid, which is the touch equivalent of zoom-to-cursor and is unconditional. A toggle would have no alternative behavior to select.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Low Definition Render: iPadRenderContext::IsLowDefinitionRender() is hard-coded to return true as a deliberate memory/perf constraint for 4 GB iPad devices. Making it a user toggle would risk OOM on large models; it's intentionally not user-configurable. Could become a pref later only if memory headroom allows full-def render on Pro devices.
- **Preferences & Settings** — xFade/xSchedule sync port: xFade and xSchedule are desktop companion apps that integrate via OS shared-memory ports (Port A/B). They don't run on iPadOS and there is no shared-memory IPC channel to another local app sandbox, so the sync-port selection has no counterpart on iPad.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Suppress Dark Mode (Windows only): Explicitly Windows-only on desktop (forces light UI vs OS dark mode); hidden on macOS/Linux already. iPadOS appearance follows the system setting (and SwiftUI honors it); there is no equivalent override and it would conflict with platform HIG.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Hardware Video Decoding: On Apple platforms video decode goes through AudioToolbox/VideoToolbox (hardware) automatically; there's no FFmpeg software-vs-hardware decode switch to expose on iPad. The desktop toggle exists to pick between FFmpeg backends, which iPad doesn't use. (Note the known VideoToolbox H.264 4:4:4 small-dims limitation is handled in core, not via a user toggle.)
- **Preferences & Settings** — Hardware Video Renderer (Windows): Windows-only choice of DirectX11/CUDA/QSV/Vulkan/AMF decode backends; hidden on macOS/Linux already. None of these backends exist on iPadOS, which uses VideoToolbox.
- **Preferences & Settings** — GPU Rendering: Desktop gates GPU rendering on Metal-compute support and lets the user opt in. On iPad the render context is already configured for the device's capabilities (low-def render, ShaderEffect via ANGLE/GLES on Metal); there is no meaningful CPU-vs-GPU render toggle to expose, and forcing CPU rendering would only hurt. Could be revisited if iPad ever offers full-def GPU compute as an option.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Shaders on Background Threads: Already hidden on macOS/Linux on desktop. Per project memory (ANGLE/GLES ShaderEffect), iPad runs ShaderEffect single-threaded on Metal via ANGLE by design; background-thread shader rendering is not applicable to the iPad's GLES-on-Metal path.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Video Export Codec: There is no video-export feature on iPad (the capability map shows preview image export by capturing the MTKView, but no encoded-video export pipeline, and the bridge notes 'iPad cannot transcode video — desktop-only'). With no video export, a codec choice has nothing to configure. If H.264/H.265 export via AVAssetWriter is added later, this becomes in-scope.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Video Export Bitrate: Same as Video Export Codec — no video-export pipeline on iPad, so there is no bitrate to set. Tied to a future AVAssetWriter-based export feature.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Tip Of The Day minimum level: There is no Tip Of The Day feature on iPad (no tips engine in src-iPad). With no tips shown, a minimum-difficulty-level choice has nothing to govern. Would only become relevant if a tips system is ported, which is itself low priority.
- **Preferences & Settings** — Tip Of The Day recycle tips: No Tip Of The Day feature on iPad, so there are no seen-tips to recycle. Dependent on porting the tips system (low priority).
- **Preferences & Settings** — Use custom color picker (experimental): Desktop's experimental toggle chooses between the OS-native color dialog and xLights' custom wx color picker. iPad uses SwiftUI's native ColorPicker (and inline ColorCurve editors) throughout; there is no wx custom-picker to switch to, so the toggle has no alternative. The native iOS picker is the correct platform choice.
- **AI Features** — AI plugin DLL loading: iOS App Store policy forbids loading executable code (dylib/DLL) from outside the signed app bundle; dynamic third-party provider plugins cannot ship on iPad. Documented in the bridge header.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — Automation port preference (Disabled / Port A / Port B): This preference only exists to configure the A/B HTTP listener and -a/-b launch flags. iPad has no command-line argv (verified: no cmdLine/argc/argv in src-iPad) and no listener; the dual A/B port scheme exists so two desktop instances + xFade/xSchedule can coexist on one machine, which is not an iPad scenario.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — Command: exportVideoPreview: Desktop encodes the preview to MP4/H.264 via FFmpeg's encoder. iPad does NOT bundle the FFmpeg encode path (bridge explicitly documents 'iPad cannot transcode video — desktop-only' via VideoTranscoder), and on-device H.264 would have to go through AVFoundation/VideoToolbox, a non-trivial separate encoder pipeline.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — Command: playJukebox: The Jukebox is a desktop panel (jukeboxPanel) for storing/triggering saved effects; no Jukebox panel exists on iPad (no jukebox UI or bridge surface found). Without the Jukebox feature itself the play-by-index command has nothing to drive.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — Command: jukeboxButtonTooltips / jukeboxButtonEffectPresent: Depends on the desktop Jukebox panel which does not exist on iPad. No data source to report tooltips/effect-present from.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — Command: closexLights: iOS apps cannot programmatically terminate themselves (Apple HIG/App Store: calling exit() is rejected; the OS owns app lifecycle). There is no equivalent of posting wxID_EXIT.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — Internal automation request helper (xLightsRequest): A wx helper (wxUtilities.cpp) that builds a URL to the local automation port and issues a request, used so xLights' own components/companion apps can drive automation over HTTP. iPad has no automation port and drives the core directly via the in-process XLSequenceDocument bridge, making an HTTP self-call pointless.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — Python scripting engine (pybind11 / embedded CPython): Embedding CPython on iOS is barred in practice: App Store guideline 2.5.2 forbids downloading/executing code that changes app behavior, and a general-purpose Python interpreter that runs arbitrary user .py files runs afoul of that; CPython/pybind11 are also not provided in the iOS deps (confirmed: no python lib in lib-ios). Desktop already compiles it only when Python.h is present.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — Run Scripts: View Script / Open Folder context menu: Desktop opens the script in the system editor and reveals the containing folder in Finder. iOS has no concept of 'reveal in Finder' or a registered external text editor for an arbitrary file; the Files app share/quick-look is the closest idiom.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — xlDo command-line tool: xlDo is a standalone CLI binary (separate target, not built for iOS) that talks to a running xLights over its localhost automation port. iOS has no shell/CLI for users to invoke a binary, no general process spawning, and no automation port on iPad. The whole tool presupposes a desktop/server environment.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — xlDo: template files with %P1..%P9 parameter substitution: A feature of the xlDo CLI (parameter substitution into a JSON template before sending over the automation port). No CLI, no template-invocation surface, and no automation port on iPad.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — xlDo: -s output script generation (set/EXPORT vars): Writes returned JSON values into a shell/batch script (set/EXPORT) for a calling shell to consume. There is no shell environment on iOS to consume such output.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — xlDo: startxLights launcher command: Launches the xLights executable on a chosen port (platform-specific exec) and polls until it responds. iOS does not allow one app to exec/launch another app's binary or pass launch flags; app launching goes through the OS, and there are no automation ports.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — App launch: headless render (-r) and check-sequence (-cs): iOS apps have no command-line argv and cannot run headless/exit-on-completion (no UI session = no app on iOS; the OS terminates background-only foreground apps, and self-exit is forbidden). Verified: no cmdLine/argc/argv handling in src-iPad.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — App launch: -a/-b port, -o output-on, -s/-m dirs, -w wipe: All are command-line switches; iOS provides no argv to the app. Show/media dirs, output-on, and settings reset are all reachable through the iPad UI (FolderConfigView, output toggle), just not via launch flags.
- **Automation, Scripting & REST API** — Internal automation request helper (xLightsRequest): A wx helper (wxUtilities.cpp) that builds a URL to the local automation port and issues a request, used so xLights' own components/companion apps can drive automation over HTTP. iPad has no automation port and drives the core directly via the in-process XLSequenceDocument bridge, making an HTTP self-call pointless.
- **Jukebox, Effect Presets & Effect Tree** — Jukebox tooltip/state export for xSchedule: This surface (SetLabel('XLIGHTS_JUKEBOX'), pipe/JSON tooltip+state strings, EVT_PLAYJUKEBOXITEM) exists solely so the desktop xSchedule companion app can read the panel via wx label introspection. xSchedule has moved to its own repo and there is no xSchedule on iPad, so this inter-app IPC contract has no consumer on iOS.
